In re Garbev Zoning Case


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


385 Pa. 328; 122 A.2d 682; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 475


Argued May 1, 1956  
May 21, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 159, Jan. T., 1956, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Dec. T., 1954, No. 789, in re: Appeal of Garbev, Inc. from Decision of Board of Adjustment of Township of Upper Darby. Decree affirmed.

Appeal by property owner from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing application for building permit. Before DIGGINS, J.

Adjudication filed finding for applicant; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered directing permit to issue. Township appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; each party to pay its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed exceptions to the adjudication, entered a finding for appellee property owner/applicant and entered a final decree directing the township to issue a building permit to the applicant.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the application for rezoning from residential use to business use, a majority of the land in question had been zoned for business use. The applicant sought a building permit in order to construct businesses and the building inspector refused to issue the permit. The Board of Adjustment denied the appeal. The lower court took testimony, sustained the appeal and concluded that the zoning ordinance was, as to the tract of land in question, arbitrary, discriminatory, confiscatory and therefore unconstitutional, and ordered the township to issue the permit. The township argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding of the lower court. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that because the evidence indicated that the land was not fit for residential purposes, and because the enforcement of the zoning ordinance would impose an unnecessary hardship on the tract of land, the owner was entitled to have a permit issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree of the lower court.

 

402 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Schultz v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


385 Pa. 79; 122 A.2d 279; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 439


Argued April 16, 1956  
April 20, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 221 and 222, Jan. T., 1956, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1956, No. 314, and Court of Common Pleas No. 3, March T., 1956, No. 372, in cases of Edward A. Schultz v. City of Philadelphia et al.; and Harry K. Butcher v. City of Philadelphia et al. Decree affirmed.

Actions in equity, consolidated.

Decree entered granting preliminary injunction, opinion by BOK, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons thus stated we affirm the decree of the court below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Philadelphia (city) sought review of judgments from the Courts of Common Pleas Nos. 3 and 6 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that granted preliminary injunctions against the city in actions brought by appellees citizens that challenged the procedure used to amend the city's charter.


OVERVIEW: The trial courts held that two amendments in a resolution adopted by the city council were defective because they failed to meet the requirements of § 2-201 of the city's charter in the advertisement and holding of public hearings. The original resolution was amended, with no further advertisement or public hearing being held, to exclude the employees of the mayor's office from its provisions, thereby differentiating such employees from those of other elective offices and assimilating them to the employees of appointive offices as to civil service and political activity. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial courts. The court upheld the trial courts' findings that the proposed change concerning employees of the mayor's office was a substantial one, more particularly because it destroyed the uniformity of the class of offices to which the amendments originally were intended to apply. The court further held that the amendments themselves were invalid because the legislature in granting the right to amend the city's charter did not grant the power asserted by the city because the legislature did not possess such power and could not itself enact this same measure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grants of preliminary injunction by the trial courts against the two amendments in the original resolution adopted by the city council.

 

403 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Addison


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


385 Pa. 48; 122 A.2d 272; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 436


Argued January 11, 1956  
April 16, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, no. 324, Jan. T., 1955, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, sept. T., 1954, No. 2707, in re: George E. Addison. Order reversed; reargument refused April 30, 1956.

Appeal by police officer from decision of Civil Service Commission affirming dismissal by police commissioner.

Appeal sustained and order entered directing reinstatement of police officer, opinion by DAVIS, J. City of Philadelphia appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed and the decision of the Civil Service Commission reinstated at the cost of the City.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police officer filed an action challenging the Civil Service Commission's (commission) decision affirming the police commissioner's decision terminating the police officer. The Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) entered an order reinstating the police officer. The city challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The police officer was dismissed by the police officer for conduct unbecoming an officer in that he had accepted a mortgage loan from a well-known numbers banker. At a hearing, it was established beyond question that the loan was for the full purchase price of a residence property. The commission later concluded that the police officer's dismissal was for just cause. On appeal, the court held that the issue was whether the scope of review by a trial court from an appeal from an order of the commission was governed by § 7-201 of the City's Home Rule Charter or by the Act of September 29, 1951, P.L. 1654. The court held that the dismissals of employees, subject to civil service, are accorded but a limited court review except for a dismissal made for ulterior reasons. In other words, the decisions of the commission are ordinarily final and not reviewable on the merits by any court. Moreover, the court held that since there were no jurisdictional or procedural grounds for granting the appeal on the commission's decision, the trial court erred in granting the police officer's request of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision reinstating the police officer in the police officer's suit challenging the commission's decision affirming the police commissioner's decision to terminate him.

 

404 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Hallmark Productions, Inc. v. Carroll


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


384 Pa. 348; 121 A.2d 584; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 564


Argued January 6, 1956  
March 13, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 345, Jan. T., 1954, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1953, No. 9265, in case of Hallmark Productions, Inc. v. Edna R. Carroll, John Clyde Fisher and Beatrice Z. Miller, of Pennsylvania State Board of Censors. Order affirmed.

Appeal by producer from decision of Board of Censors refusing certificate of approval for motion picture film.

Order entered sustaining appeal, opinion by LEWIS, P.J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Pennsylvania State Board of Censors (board), sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which reversed a decision of the board that refused to issue a certificate of approval for a motion picture film to appellee movie producer.


OVERVIEW: A movie producer submitted to the board for approval a motion picture film, which presented the story of a dope peddler and the manner in which he enticed innocent people in the use and sale of marijuana cigarettes. The board found that the film was indecent and immoral and, in the judgment of the board, tended to debase and corrupt morals, and therefore disapproved it. The court of common pleas reversed. The sole issue on appeal was whether the Motion Picture Censorship Act of May 15, 1915, 1915 Pa. Laws 534, as amended by 1929 Pa. Laws 1655, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the law was unconstitutional. The court held that, under the First and Fourteenth Amendments, a state could not ban a film on the basis of the board's conclusion that it was "indecent and immoral." The court found that motion pictures were protected by the free speech and free press guarantees of the First and Fourteenth Amendments. The court held that, assuming that a state could establish a system for the licensing of motion pictures, a court's duty was to examine the facts of the refusal in each case and determine whether the principles of the First Amendment were honored.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal by court of common pleas of the board's decision, which had refused to issue a certificate of approval for a motion picture film to the movie producer.

 

405 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania R. Co. v. Schwartz


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


383 Pa. 575; 119 A.2d 314; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 633


Argued November 17, 1955  
January 4, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 8 and 9, May T., 1940, in case of Pennsylvania Railroad Company v. Leon Schwartz et al., substituted defendants. Petition dismissed without prejudice.

Proceeding on petition filed in the Supreme Court by the Attorny General designated "Bill of Review to Amend and Modify Final Decree."

On June 2, 1937, the plaintiff filed a bill in equity in the Court of Common Pleas Of Dauphin County alleging that sections, 2, 4, 5, 6, 7 and 8 of the "full crew" Act of June 1, 1937, P.L. 1120, were unconstitutional. The plaintiff prayed that (1) these sections be adjudged void, (2) that the Public Utility Commission and the Attorney General be enjoined "from enforcing the provisions of said Sections of said Act," and (3) general relief.

On March 15, 1939, the chancellor entered a decree nisi permanently enjoining the Public Utility Commission and the Attorney General, or their successors in office, "from enforcing the Full Crew Act approved June 1, 1937, P.L. 1120, or otherwise interfering with the plaintiff in the operation of its railroad in the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania because of failure to comply with any of the provisions of the said Act." Exceptions were dismissed [***2] and the final decree, in the same words, was entered on April 26, 1939. The Supreme Court affirmed this final decree on November 27, 1939: Pennsylvania Railroad Co. v. Driscoll et al., 336 Pa. 310. No petition for reargument or modification of order was filed.

In June 1955 the successor Attorney General filed the present petition, alleging "That, by reason of the severability provisions of Section 13 of said Act, those sections not passed upon in the opinions of the court below and of Your Honorable Court are not impaired and remain in full force and effect;" and that the scope of the decree, in enjoining enforcement of the Act in its entirety (particularly §§ 3 and 9) constituted "an error of law apparent in the decree itself." The petition prayed that the order of the Supreme Court affirming the final decree "be reviewed, modified and amended," so that the restraining effect of the decree "shall apply to only those portions of the Act ... which are declared to be unconstitutional, without interfering with the enforcement of the remaining and constitutional sections of said Act."

The plaintiff filed an answer, denying "that the final decree is erroneous in any respect" and [***3] asked for the dismissal of this proceeding.

 

406 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Barth v. Gorson


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


383 Pa. 611; 119 A.2d 309; 1956 Pa. LEXIS 637


Argued December 1, 1955  
January 4, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 246, Jan. T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1954, No. 2518, in case of Paul A. Barth, Jr., et ux. v. Joseph N. Gorson, Joseph S. Clark, Jr., Mayor of City of Philadelphia, et al. Decree affirmed.

Equity.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and final decree entered dismissing complaint, opinion by DAVIS, J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is affirmed at cost of the appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner complained of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the owner's complaint seeking equitable relief from a zoning change granted on defendant neighboring property owner's land.


OVERVIEW: The property owner complained that the change in the zoning classification of the neighboring owner's property from residential to commercial should be overturned and the zoning ordinance declared unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court ruled that a court of equity had no jurisdiction to interfere in the lawful exercise of a statutory process, unless that process involved clearly illegal acts. The court held that the authority of a city council to enact zoning ordinances and to provide a mechanism for appeals of zoning decisions was granted by statute. As such, the statutory processes enacted must be followed strictly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the property owner's complaint that sought equitable relief from a zoning change granted on a neighbor's property.

Berks County Institution Dist. v. Schoener


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


383 Pa. 210; 117 A.2d 740; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 343


Argued October 6, 1955  
November 14, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 178 and 186, Jan. T., 1955, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Nov. T., 1952, No. 44, in cases of Berks County Institution District v. Ralph E. Schoener. Appeal by defendant dismissed; appeal by plaintiff sustained and judgment modified.

Assumpsit. Before SHANAMAN, J.

Verdict directed for plaintiff; defendant's motion for judgment n.o.v. granted in part and final order entered granting plaintiff judgment in a reduced amount. Plaintiff and defendant, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The appeal of the Institution District to No. 186 January Term, 1955 is sustained, and the judgment entered by the court below is modified with instructions to that court to enter judgment upon the verdict of the jury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Berks County Institution District appealed a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania), which partially granted judgment notwithstanding the verdict to appellee county controller by reducing the amount of the verdict returned in favor of the District. The controller appealed that portion of the verdict not included in the judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: The District brought an action against the controller to recover the amount of expenses he received in connection with the duties of his office. The controller's reports did not show any actual expenses incurred in connection with the District nor were actual expense accounts submitted to the District. The jury returned a verdict for the District for the full amount of its claim and the controller filed a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The trial court partially granted the motion by reducing the amount of the award to reflect the expenses shown for the controller on his successor's report. Both parties appealed and the court sustained the appeal of the district and directed the trial court to modify the decision by entering judgment for the full amount of the jury verdict. The court found 1949 P.L. 1709 (Pennsylvania), codified at Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 62, § 2253, which allowed a lump sum for the controller's expenses, unconstitutional. As such the District was entitled to reimbursement for any undocumented expenses. The expenses allowed by the trial court were not in connection with any statutory duties of the controller for the District.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the appeal of the District and modified the decision with instructions for the trial court to enter judgment upon the jury's verdict.

Commonwealth ex rel. Woodside v. Sun Ray Drug Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


383 Pa. 1; 116 A.2d 833; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 303


Argued April 28, 1955  
September 26, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 21, May T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, in Equity, No. 2045, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Robert E. Woodside, Attorney General v. Sun Ray Drug Company and Carlo Galletta and Richard Nasuti, trading as Carl-Rich. Decree reversed.

Equity. Before KREIDER, J.

Adjudication filed awarding injunctive relief against defendants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final order entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is reversed, costs to be paid by the intervenor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant drug company appealed from a decree by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which granted the Commonwealth's motion seeking injunctive relief against the drug company.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth and the ice cream manufacturers, as the intervenor, brought the action in equity to enjoin the drug company from violating the Pennsylvania Ice Cream Law, Act of May 20, 1949, P.L. 1594, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 407 et seq. The state contended that the drug company possessed and intended to sell a product alleged to be an inferior simulation of ice cream. The drug company appealed from an order that enjoined the drug company from selling the frozen sweetened milk product referred to as malt-a-plenty and shake-o-malt. On appeal, the court stated that because the Pennsylvania Ice Cream Law did not regulate the sale of milk shakes or establish any standard for the ingredients of a milk shake, sales of the malt-a-plenty drink did not constitute a violation of the statute. Thus, in the absence of any evidence of customer confusion between malt-a-plenty base and ice cream and of any sales of malt-a-plenty base as ice cream, its possession or manufacture could not be restrained. The court concluded that police power could be exercised only in the public interest and could not be used as a device to restrain fair competition.


OUTCOME: The decree of was reversed, costs to be paid by the intervenor.

 

409 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Berner v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 622; 116 A.2d 738; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 439


Argued May 25, 1955  
September 26, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 163, Jan. T., 1955, from order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania affirming the order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission at Application Docket No. 15845, in case of Clyde E. Berner et al. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Order reversed.

Same case in Superior Court: 177 Pa. Super. Ct. 19.

Proceeding before the Public Utility Commission upon complaints against proposed increased rates of telephone company.

Order entered dismissing complaints and approving proposed rates. Claimants appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the order of the commission. Appeal by claimants to Supreme Court allowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ratepayers sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania affirming the order of appellee Utility Commission, which dismissed the ratepayers' complaints and approved the telephone company's proposed rate increases.


OVERVIEW: When the telephone company requested approval for a rate increase from the Utility Commission, the ratepayers filed complaints protesting the increase. After a hearing, the Commission issued an order dismissing the complaint and approving the increase, which the superior court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the superior court, ruling that the evidence did not support the Commission's findings and that the company failed to show that the increase was reasonably necessary as required by § 701(c) of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Law. The court determined that payments made to affiliates by the telephone company for services were improperly included in the rate base because the company failed to show that these expenses were reasonably necessary and that they were not excessive. Further, the cost of materials stockpiled for future use were improperly included because the equipment that the stored materials would replace was already included. The court ruled that the estimated fair rate of return was not reasonable because it was calculated based on the stock offerings of companies that were not in a financial position comparable to that of the company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court affirming the order of the Utility Commission, which dismissed the ratepayers' complaints and approved the telephone company's proposed rate increases. The court remanded the case to the Utility Commission for further proceedings and with direction to make proper findings on the basis of further evidence.

Sherwood v. Elgart


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


383 Pa. 110; 117 A.2d 899; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 321; 63 A.L.R.2d 490


Argued September 30, 1954; reargued May 2, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 222 and 223, Jan. T., 1954, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 4, June T., 1952, No. 2821; Nos. 224 and 225, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 7, Sept. T., 1952, No. 5134; Nos. 226 and 227, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 7, Dec. T., 1952, No. 3990; Nos. 228 and 229, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 3, March T., 1953, No. 3186; and Nos. 272 and 273, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 4, March T., 1953, No. 6643, in case of Florence Sherwood, Antionette Rosenberger, George Landis, Wuanita Smith and Alberta Porter v. Samuel Elgart, Clinton Management, Inc., etc. Judgments reversed; further reargument refused November 28, 1955.

Actions of trespass for property damages. Before BOK, P.J., without a jury.

Verdicts for plaintiffs and judgments entered thereon. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed, and here entered for the respective defendants non obstante veredicto.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hotel owners and operators sought review of a decision by the Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which entered judgement in favor of plaintiff hotel guests in the guests' action for property damages allegedly due to a trespass by the owners and operators.


OVERVIEW: A fire destroyed the hotel run by the owners and operators. The guests brought a trespass action, charging various acts of negligence, and seeking damages for personal property alleged to have been lost in the fire. The lower court entered judgment in favor of the guests. Upon appeal, the court reversed and entered a judgment non obstante veredicto in favor of the owners and operators. The court found that § 4 of the Act of June 12, 1913, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 37, § 61 et seq., precluded a recovery for such losses. The court found that the legislature had clearly exempted a hotel proprietor for loss of personal property which was kept in the guests' rooms and was destroyed by an unintentional fire.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment entered in favor of the guests.

 

411 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Burche Co. v. General Electric Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 370; 115 A.2d 361; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 409C


Argued May 24, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 24, May T., 1955, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Sept. T., 1952, No. 310, in case of Burche Co. v. General Electric Company and Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Judgment affirmed.

Declaratory judgment proceeding.

Judgment entered in favor of defendant, opinion by KREIDER, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed at the cost of the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a retail store operator, sought review of a judgment entered in the Court of Common Pleas, Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) for defendant manufacturer and intervening defendant the Commonwealth in a declaratory judgment action. The operator claimed that because it did not sign a fair trade agreement with the manufacturer the Act of 1935, P.L. 266 as amended by the Act of 1941, P.L. 128, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 7 did not apply to it.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer engaged in price regulation of its commodities by means of a minimum retail price agreement commonly known as fair trade contracts and had entered into such agreements with other retailers that did business in the Commonwealth. The operator claimed that because it had not entered into a fair trade agreement with the manufacturer the Act as applied to it was unconstitutional. The court affirmed. Generally fair trade acts were held constitutional. The Act was not an unlawful delegation of legislative power and in fact was not a delegation of power at all. At the time the Act was passed and amended it was unconstitutional as applied to interstate commerce because it conflicted with the Sherman Anti-Trust Act, but the prohibition was later removed. The Act was clearly in force as to intrastate commerce and where a state statute was declared unconstitutional or invalid because it was in conflict with federal legislation, the repeal of the federal statute reinstated or revived the state law without an express re-enactment by the state legislature. The Act applied to nonsignatories in interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

412 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 380; 115 A.2d 218; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 411


Argued May 2, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 201, 202 and 200, Jan. T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1954, Nos. 6327, 6420 and 6518, in cases of John Warren and Property Owners Association of Philadelphia, Inc. and Queen Lane Village, Inc., and Queen Lane Manor, Inc., intervenors, v. City of Philadelphia, George Braeunig, Jr. v. City of Philadelphia, and Frank Giacobbo et al. v. City of Philadelphia. Decree reversed.

Complaints in equity.

Plaintiffs' motion for judgment on the pleadings granted, opinion by ALESSANDRONI, J. City appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed with a procedendo; costs to abide the event.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review after the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) declared the Philadelphia Rent Control Ordinance unconstitutional and void. Plaintiff landlords sought a permanent injunction declaring the rent control ordinance void and restraining enforcement of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The landlords sought a permanent injunction declaring the city's rent control ordinance void. The city filed an answer to the complaint in equity. On motion for judgment on the pleadings, the trial court declared the ordinance unconstitutional and void. The trial court held that it was in conflict with various acts of assembly of the commonwealth and that the city had no police power to enact rent controls. The court reversed. The court held that § 17 of the First Class City Home Rule Act of 1949 authorized the city to enact ordinances, rules, and regulations necessary to execute powers relating to its municipal functions. The Rent Commission acted in an administrative capacity, as did zoning boards, and the exercise of those powers was not in violation of Pa. Const. art. V, § 1. The ordinance did not conflict with the Landlord and Tenant Act because the ordinance did not touch upon substantive law as to when a landlord had the right to evict. Where both a state statute and a municipal ordinance legislated as to the same subjects, both were upheld if they were not in conflict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree that found a rent control ordinance unconstitutional and void.

 

413 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. American Tel. & Tel. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 509; 115 A.2d 373; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 429


Argued May 23, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 16, May T., 1955, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1953, No. 200, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. American Telephone and Telegraph Company. Judgment affirmed.

Appeal by corporation from action of Board of Finance and Revenue refusing to resettle corporate net income tax settlement.

Appeal sustained and judgment entered for corporation, opinion by RICHARDS, P.J., specially presiding. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which held that the proper amount of corporate net income tax for appellee telephone company was $ 24,602.


OVERVIEW: The instant controversy hinged on the sole question of whether the corporate net income tax should be applied against the telephone company on a unitary or on a multiform basis. Under the unitary basis the telephone company's tax would have been $ 24,602 whereas under the multiform basis the tax would have been $ 237,756. On appeal, the court held that the Corporate Net Income Tax Act was not unconstitutional. The court found that the activities of the telephone company were conducted by two separate and unrelated units. The court also found that the Corporate Net Income Tax Act made no reference to, or provision for, any division of a corporation into different departmental units. The court reasoned that it was clear that Corporate Net Income Tax Act neither expressly nor impliedly provided for a computation of the tax on any other than a unitary basis, making no differentiation in the case of corporations carrying on multiform activities. Thus, the court ruled that the telephone company was entitled to computation of its net income tax on a unitary basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the $ 24, 602 net income tax assessment.

 

414 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Schmidt v. Philadelphia Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 521; 114 A.2d 902; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 431


Argued April 26, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 135, Jan. T., 1955, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1954, No. 950, in case of John G. Schmidt et al. v. Philadelphia Zoning Board of Adjustment and American Meter Company. Order affirmed.

Appeal by objecting property owner from decision of Philadelphia Zoning Board of Adjustment confirming action of Department of Licenses and Inspections in issuing zoning and use permits for industrial use of property. Before SPORKIN, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal. Objecting property owner appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is affirmed; costs on this appeal to be borne by the City.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review on a writ of certiorari of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's appeal from an order of appellee city board of adjustment. The board affirmed a city's issuance of zoning and use permits to intervenor property owner pursuant to a city ordinance enacted under the Act of May 6, 1929, P. L. 1551 (Pennsylvania).


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that the amendatory ordinance under which the intervenor's permits were issued constituted illegal "spot zoning." The property in question was originally zoned for general industrial use. After 18 years, the classification of the subject property was changed to a residential category. One year later, the city, through an amendatory ordinance, again reclassified the property as general industrial. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant sought review on a writ of certiorari, and the scope of the court's review was limited to whether the trial court's decision was based on sufficient evidence, whether there was a flagrant abuse of discretion, and whether the decision was free from a violation of positive law. The trial court correctly dismissed the appeal, and the evidence supported the decision below. The challenged ordinance did not constitute "spot zoning," and was not an unconstitutional use of the city's police power. The city had the authority under § 5 of the enabling Act of May 6, 1929, P. L. 1551 (Pennsylvania) to amend its zoning ordinances and to reclassify the subject property's use classification, which was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the appeal by appellant from the order of the board, which affirmed the city's issuance of zoning and use permits to intervenor.

 

415 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Ewalt v. Pennsylvania Turnpike Com.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 529; 115 A.2d 729; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 432


Argued May 25, 1955  
June 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 23, May T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 2115, Equity Docket 130, Commonwealth Docket 1954, in case of H. Ward Ewalt, Jr., et ux. v. Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission. Decree reversed.

Equity.

Decree entered dismissing bill; opinion by RICHARDS, P.J., specially presiding. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is reversed with a procedendo at the costs of the appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decree from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objection of appellee Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission and dismissed the owners' equitable action to compel the Commission to restore their property to its condition prior to the Commission's construction of the western extension of the turnpike.


OVERVIEW: The Commission constructed the western extension of the Pennsylvania turnpike pursuant to the Western Pennsylvania Turnpike Extension Act of 1941, codified at Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 36, § 654 et seq. Under the Act a right of action was given to public or private owners of property for damage or destruction caused by the Commission during the construction authorized therein. The owners brought an equitable action to compel the Commission to restore their property to its condition prior to such construction, alleging that the construction caused dirt, rocks, and other debris to fill a lake located on the owner's property. The trial court sustained the Commission's preliminary objections and dismissed the action, holding that the Act was unconstitutional because its title did not advise the Commission of the liability imposed upon it therein. The owners appealed and the court reversed, finding that the damage to the owners' property arose from the Commission's activity under the Act, which also authorized the owners' action for damages. The title of the Act was sufficient to embrace the provision that imposed liability for property damage upon the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree that dismissed the owners' action.

 

416 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. County of Allegheny


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


382 Pa. 88; 114 A.2d 491; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 381


Argued June 3, 1954; reargued March 22, 1955  
May 23, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 185 to 190, inclusive, and 193 to 221, inclusive, March T., 1954, from decrees of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Oct. T., 1953, Nos. 1288, 1289, 1640, 1706 and 1707, in cases of K. C. Gardner et ux. v. County of Allegheny, Trans World Airlines, Inc., et al.; Helen May Springer v. Same; Elizabeth B. M. Gardner and Kirtland C. Gardner, Jr. v. Same; Nancy Springer Patton v. Same, and Thomas N. Griggs v. Same. Decree modified and, as modified, affirmed.

Equity.

Decree entered dismissing defendants' preliminary objections, before SOFFEL, DUFF, and WEISS, JJ., opinion per curiam. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree as thus modified is affirmed and the lower Court is directed to enter a modified decree consistent with this Opinion and to grant such further relief as to it may seem proper. Each party shall pay his or its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) overruled the preliminary objections of defendants, a county and several airlines, to the complaint of plaintiff landowners that alleged continuing trespasses to their land and a taking of their respective properties and that sought an injunction or damages. The county and airlines appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned certain tracts of land located in defendant county. The landowners alleged in their complaint that in landing upon and taking off from the airport, the airlines' planes descended and ascended along a glide angle that was below the floor of the navigable air space and about fifteen to thirty feet above the chimneys of their respective houses, thereby causing them to suffer from noises, vibrations, lights, and other nuisances. The airlines and county's preliminary objections contended that the trial court, which was sitting in equity, lacked jurisdiction because of the absence of indispensable parties, namely the Civil Aeronautics Board and Administrator (board and administrator). The county also maintained that the court lacked jurisdiction over the cause of action. The appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that: (1) the board and administrator were not necessary and indispensable parties; (2) the trial court sitting in equity had jurisdiction to enjoin repeated trespasses on the landowners' property; and (3) the trial court sitting in equity had no jurisdiction to determine or assess damages for a taking of the landowners' property.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decree, affirmed the decree as so modified, and directed the trial court to enter a consistent modified decree and grant such further relief as seemed proper.

Jameson v. Pittsburgh


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


381 Pa. 366; 113 A.2d 454; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 491


Argued November 12, 1954  
April 18, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 290, March T., 1954, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Oct. T., 1953, No. 3255, in case of J. H. Jameson v. City of Pittsburgh et al. Order affirmed; reargument refused May 3, 1955.

Bill in equity.

Defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings refused, before MARSHALL, O'BRIEN and DUGG, JJ., opinion by O'BRIEN, J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, costs to abide the event.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which refused its motion for judgment on the pleadings in plaintiff taxpayer's action to enjoin the city from taking any action pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 9414(d) (1953).


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer sought to enjoin the city from taking any action pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 9414(d) (1953). Section 9414(d) authorized the pension board to establish a program whereby a beneficiary who paid $ 200 into the pension fund received an additional annuity in addition to his regular pension. The city appealed the refusal of its motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court affirmed because § 9414(d) violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 11, as to the employees retired at the time its passage. The court found that the city's moral obligation to provide adequate allowance to pensioners was insufficient to sustain its right to change the retirement allowances. The court found that the voluntary contribution of $ 200 did not remove § 9414(d) from the constitutional prohibition against extra compensation after services were rendered because the increased pension was still a gratuitous disbursement from the fund to which the pensioner was not entitled when he joined the fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with costs, the refusal of the city's motion on the pleadings in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the enforcement of the statute increasing the pension.

 

418 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Jacobs v. Fetzer


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


381 Pa. 262; 112 A.2d 356; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 477


Argued January 6, 1955  
March 23, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 48, Jan. T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, June T., 1953, in Equity, No. 952, in case of William Jacobs v. Paul L. Fetzer, et al., members of Council of Ridley Park Borough, et al. Decree reversed.

Bill in equity. Before TOAL, J.

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiff and enjoining enforcement of zoning ordinance; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and bill dismissed at the appellee's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the members of the borough council, the burgess, and the secretary of the council, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee landowner, in the landowner's action to enjoin the zoning ordinance as unconstitutional, illegal, and void, insofar as it classified the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The landowner bought undeveloped lots, on which he hoped to build two family houses. The zoning ordinance only permitted one family houses on that property. The landowner petitioned the borough council to reclassify the property. The council refused the petition. The landowner then brought an action in equity against the burgess, the members of the council, and the secretary of the council. The trial court declared the ordinance unconstitutional as applied to the landowner. On the appeal of the council and the others, the court reviewed the record and held that the trial court had erred in hearing the case. The court determined that the complaint should have been dismissed for want of jurisdiction over the subject matter. The zoning ordinance was properly enacted pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 15211.1 et seq. (1947). The ordinance provided that a party challenging a zoning decision had to bring the issue before a board of adjustment in order to appeal further to the trial court. The remedies authorized by statutes had to be strictly pursued, pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 46, § 156 (1806). The landowner, however, had improperly sought a remedy from the borough council.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

419 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Smith Case


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


381 Pa. 223; 112 A.2d 625; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 472; 55 A.L.R.2d 420


Argued January 5, 1955  
March 23, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction. No. 133, Miscellaneous Docket No. 10, in re application of Harvey A. Smith for writ of prohibition directed to Judges of Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County. Substituted rule to show cause discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition to determine the constitutionality of the Act of January 14, 1952 (1952 Act), 1952 Pa. Laws 2087, amending the Act of June 16, 1836 (1836 Act), 1836 Pa. Laws 715, and the validity of Lancaster County, Pa., C.P. Ct. R. 43, adopted in pursuance of this legislation. The court denied the petition, but substituted for it a rule to show cause why a writ of mandamus should not issue.


OVERVIEW: The 1952 Act provided that the courts of common pleas could, by rules of court, require arbitration for cases where the amount in controversy was under $ 1000. The arbitrators' compensation was to be determined by the court and paid by the county; any party appealing was to first repay to the county such fees, but such fees were not to follow the award. The court held that the 1952 Act was constitutional because it allowed an appeal from the decision of the arbitrators, but that Rule 43 should be amended because it required a payment of $ 75 for the right to appeal, which would operate as a strong deterrent, amounting practically to a denial of that right, if the case should involve only a small amount in dispute. Since the 1952 Act authorized the courts to provide for compulsory arbitration in all cases where the amount in controversy was less than $ 1000, a court could not limit the submission to arbitration of cases involving less than $ 500; the system must either be adopted as an entirety and as prescribed by the 1952 Act or not at all. The court discharged the rule to show cause because neither directed amendment affected petitioner.


OUTCOME: Although the court held that the 1952 Act was constitutional and that the common pleas court rule should be amended in two respects, the court discharged the rule to show cause why a writ of mandamus should not issue directing the court to place the case on the list for trial before a jury, because petitioner was not directly affected by either of the directed amendments.

 

420 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Bernitsky v. County of Schuylkill


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


381 Pa. 128; 112 A.2d 120; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 459


Argued January 4, 1955  
March 14, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 14, Jan. T., 1955, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County, July T., 1953, No. 12, in case of Joseph Bernitsky and George Stenulis v. The County of Schuylkill, The Township of Blythe and The School District of Blythe. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition of purchasers of land and rule to show cause why redemption of property should not be allowed. Before CURRAN, J.

Order entered dismissing rule. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed at cost of appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the purchasers of the property, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Schuykill County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee county, in the action by the purchasers against appellees, the county, the township, and the school district, for a rule to show cause why redemption of the property should not be allowed.


OVERVIEW: The County Treasurer sold the grantor's land to the County Commissioners for delinquent taxes. The grantor transferred some of the land to the purchasers. The purchasers then requested the Commissioners for permission to redeem the property. After the Commissioners refused, the purchasers brought an action against the county, the township, and the school district. After the trial court dismissed the purchasers' rule to show cause why redemption should not be allowed, the purchasers appealed. The court reviewed the record and determined that the trial court had properly dismissed the rule. The court determined that the right of redemption did not exist at common law, but only by statute. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 5860.702 (1947) had repealed earlier rights of redemption when either the property was turned over to a Tax Claim Bureau or the redemption period had expired. Moreover, the purchaser had only acquired what rights the grantor had, and the grantor had wasted all rights to redemption before the sale to the purchasers, when the property had been transferred from the Commissioners to the Bureau pursuant to the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Butcher v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


380 Pa. 290; 110 A.2d 349; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 567


Argued November 23, 1954  
January 12, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 238, Jan. T., 1954, from decree of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1954, No. 1011, in case of Harry K. Butcher v. City of Philadelphia, Joseph S. Clark, Mayor, et al. Decree reversed.

Bill in equity.

Plaintiff's motion for judgment on the pleadings granted, opinion by GUERIN, J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is reversed; the parties to pay their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) that granted an injunction against implementation of the Civil Service Commission's (commission) Emergency Regulation "B" (regulation) in plaintiff taxpayer's action for declaratory and injunctive relief, alleging that the regulation was invalid in permitting former county employees to become city employees without taking the required competitive examination.


OVERVIEW: Voters passed the City-County Consolidation Amendment (amendment), which consolidated county and city offices. The commission adopted the regulation, which exempted former county employees from taking the competitive examination prescribed for city employees under the Home Rule Charter, permitting such employees to retain their positions by taking a qualifying test. Subsequent caselaw required all former county employees to become city employees and pass the competitive examination. The taxpayer thereafter filed an action alleging that the regulation was invalid and the trial court granted an injunction against its implementation. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that: 1) the commission had the discretionary power to adopt the regulation based upon the emergency situation created by the uncertainty of the effect of the amendment on the status of the former county employees; therefore, 2) subsequently decided caselaw, which required the county employees to pass the civil service exam in order to become city employees, was properly given prospective effect; and 3) the implementation of regulation prior to the legal decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which granted an injunction against implementation of the regulation, in the taxpayer's action against the city alleging that the regulation was invalid.

Commonwealth ex rel. Truscott v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


380 Pa. 367; 111 A.2d 136; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 575


Argued November 22, 1954  
January 12, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction. No. 143, Miscellaneous Docket No. 10, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Frank F. Truscott, Attorney General, and Lillian Woodard et al., v. City of Philadelphia, Joseph S. Clark, Jr., Mayor, and Vernon D. Northrop, Director of Finance, City of Philadelphia. Final decree entered enjoining City of Philadelphia officials from carrying into effect city ordinance; reargument refused February 7, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Each party shall pay its, his or their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commonwealth of Pennsylvania brought an action in equity against defendant City of Philadelphia seeking to enjoin it from enforcing an ordinance abolishing the Board of Revision of Taxes and establishing new city offices to which it transferred the former board's duties. It asserted that the city's actions violated the Pennsylvania Constitution and were an unauthorized usurpation of power.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance abolishing the Board of Revision of Taxes and established in its place a new city office to which it transferred the former board's functions. The commonwealth filed a complaint in equity to enjoin the enforcement of the ordinance as unconstitutional and an unauthorized usurpation of power. The court granted the injunction. It ruled that prior to the enactment of the City-County Consolidation Amendment (amendment), Pa. Const. art. XIV, § 8, the city had a county government and a city government. The amendment abolished all county offices and decreed that the city was to perform all functions of county government until such time as the people of the commonwealth should otherwise provide. The city sought to evade and nullify the clear language of the amendment, which was the supreme law of Pennsylvania, by contending that the amendment meant to give the city council the power to otherwise provide. The court held that such a contention was absolutely and completely devoid of merit. It concluded that the ordinance approved by the city was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the city was restrained and enjoined from enforcing the ordinance abolishing a tax board and creating city offices to assume the functions of the tax board in the action of the commonwealth for equitable relief.

 

423 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Edwards


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


380 Pa. 52; 110 A.2d 216; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 528


Argued November 8, 1954  
January 3, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 239, Jan. T., 1954, from judgment of Court of Oyer and Terminer of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1952, No. 961, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Grover Cleveland Edwards. Judgment affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with murder. Before GUERIN, J.

Verdict of guilty with penalty fixed at death and judgment of sentence thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of sentence is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Oyer and Terminer of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sole contention on appeal, was that the matters whereof he now complained helped motivate the jury in fixing the penalty at death rather than life imprisonment and that, consequently, the court should have substituted the latter penalty for the former. The court stated that it was without the lawful power to do so. Defendant charged that the trial judge (1) did not treat adequately with the evidence of drunkenness, adduced by defendant, in its relation to the question of penalty and (2) erred in admitting in evidence a statement made by the victim while being transported from the scene of the crime to the hospital. The court rejected both claims. It noted that the trial judge properly instructed the jury that, if defendant's drunkenness was such that he was incapable of forming a specific intent to take life, then the homicide could not have been raised above second degree murder. Further, the victim's statement was properly admitted under the res gestae rule. The statement emanated from the lips of the victim under the shock and excitement of the inflicted violence which impelled its utterance and so soon thereafter that the continuity was not broken.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Cott Beverage Corp. v. Horst


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


380 Pa. 113; 110 A.2d 405; 1955 Pa. LEXIS 539


Argued November 17, 1954  
January 3, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 8, May T., 1955, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1954, in Equity, No. 2105, and Commonwealth Docket No. 2, in case of Cott Beverage Corporation and Cott Bottling Co. of Pittsburgh v. Miles Horst, Secretary of Agriculture and Frank F. Truscott, Attorney General. Decree affirmed.

Bill in equity. Before RICHARDS, P.J., specially sitting

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiffs; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The final decree of the court below is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Secretary of Agriculture and attorney general, appealed a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, corporation and licensee, in their action for an injunction enjoining defendants from prohibiting plaintiffs from selling a non-alcoholic carbonated beverage and from requiring on such drinks a certain label prescribed by the Department of Agriculture.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants for an injunction enjoining defendants from prohibiting plaintiffs from selling non-alcoholic carbonated beverages containing sucaryl and no honey, sugar or dextrose, and from requiring on such drinks a certain label prescribed by the Department of Agriculture (department). The trial court granted the injunction, and defendants appealed. The court affirmed. The Act of May 14, 1925, P.L. 730 was declared unconstitutional as violative of the Fourteenth Amendment and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. The court concluded that the Act of May 13, 1909, P.L. 520 (520) did not apply to carbonated beverages and drinks because the legislature did not intend to include drinks in the term "food." The court held that since 520 did not apply to carbonated non-alcoholic drinks, the requirement of 520 that the label was to contain an appropriate warning statement prescribed by the department did not affect the product. The court found that the warning prescribed by the department was not appropriate, but wholly unreasonable and unnecessarily alarming, since it would naturally tend to discourage the purchase and use of what admittedly is a harmless product.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of an injunction in favor of plaintiffs in their action seeking to enjoin defendants from prohibiting them from selling a non-alcoholic carbonated beverage and from requiring on such drinks a certain label prescribed by the Department of Agriculture.

Holmes' Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


379 Pa. 599; 109 A.2d 523; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 383


Argued October 5, 1954  
November 23, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 245 and 280, Jan. T., 1954, from order of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1953, Nos. 138 and 139, affirming judgment of Municipal Court of Philadelphia County, No. 115670, in re Joseph Holmes, an alleged delinquent. Order affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 175 Pa. Super, Ct. 137.

Proceeding before Juvenile Court on petition alleging delinquency of minor. Before PROPPER, J.

Order entered adjudicating minor a delinquent and directing his commitment to Pennsylvania Industrial School, Juvenile appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the order of the court below. Appeal by juvenile to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Superior Court is affirmed.

The order of the Superior Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor challenged an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the juvenile court's adjudication of the minor's delinquency.


OVERVIEW: The minor was on probation when delinquency petitions were filed charging that he had driven a stolen car without a license and participated in the armed robbery of a church. The intermediate appellate court affirmed the juvenile court's commitment of the minor to a reform school. The minor claimed, inter alia, that his privilege against self-incrimination was violated; that hearsay evidence was received regarding the armed robbery charge; that he was improperly prevented from inspecting reports received by the court from probation officers; and that commitment to the reform school was improper because it also housed persons convicted of crime in a criminal court. The court affirmed. The court held that proceedings under the Juvenile Court Law were not penal but protective; constitutional rights granted to those accused of crime did not apply. Many legalistic features of the rules of evidence also did not apply in juvenile court. It was permissible to rely on ex parte information in connection with the disposition of a case in juvenile court. The fact that minors sentenced in criminal court could be committed to the reform school did not make it a prison.


OUTCOME: The court held that the minor was properly committed to reform school. The court affirmed the adjudication of the minor's delinquency.

Appeal of Catholic Cemeteries Asso.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


379 Pa. 516; 109 A.2d 537; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 376


Argued October 5, 1954  
November 22, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 281, March T., 1954, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, 1953, No. A-840, in Appeal of Catholic Cemeteries Association of the Diocese of Pittsburgh et al. Order reversed; reargument refused December 17, 1954.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Zoning Board of Adjustment refusing to grant exception or variance for cemetery purposes. Before LENCHER, P.J.

Adjudication filed sustaining appeal; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final order entered. Township appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed, at cost of appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of the order from the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which directed the Board of Adjustment of Upper St. Clair Township to grant a certificate and permits to appellees, Catholic Cemeteries Association and others (association), for the use of approximately 185 acres of land in the township as a cemetery.


OVERVIEW: The association sought to amend an ordinance in order to permit a cemetery in the township. The board of supervisors refused to amend the ordinance. The board of adjustment upheld the decision because the requested use was not within those permitted for single family dwellings. It also found that to grant such permit as an exception or a variance would constitute a re-zoning of the district that was beyond the power of the board. The trial court reversed the decision and ordered the board of adjustment to grant the desired certificate and permits. The trial court found that literal enforcement of the provisions of the ordinance would result in unnecessary hardships, and that the variance was not contrary to the public interest. The township contended that the lower court did not properly exercise its reviewable powers. The court reversed and found that it was error to direct the issuance of the requested certificates and permits. The court held that to grant a variance for an area of 185 acres would, in effect, constitute a re-zoning of the area. There was also no evidence in the record to support the finding that to deny the requested use would result in unnecessary hardship.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that directed the issuance of a certificate and permits for a cemetery in the township. The court found that there was no evidence to support the finding of the trial court that a denial of the use as a cemetery would result in unnecessary hardship. It was error to direct the issuance of the requested certificate and permits.

Commonwealth v. Budd Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


379 Pa. 159; 108 A.2d 563; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 339


Argued January 12, 1954  
June 28, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 8 and 9, May T., 1954, from judgments of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1949 and 1950, Commonwealth Docket Nos. 7 and 31, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. The Budd Company, and Same v. Westinghouse Electric Corporation. Judgments affirmed; reargument refused November 9, 1954.

Appeal by taxpayer from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue refusing petition for review of resettlement of corporate net income taxes. Before SMITH, P.J., without a jury.

Adjudication entered finding for taxpayer; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and judgment entered for taxpayer. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in each case is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this consolidated appeal of two cases, appellant commonwealth challenged the judgments from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which ruled in favor of appellee taxpayers, dismissed the commonwealth's exceptions to adjudication, and entered judgment for the taxpayers. The taxpayers brought their actions to challenge their assessed corporate net income tax.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth contended that § 2 of the Corporate Net Income Tax Act of May 14, 1947, codified at 1947 Pa. Laws 232, was constitutional in its application to the taxpayers' 1944 corporate net income. The commonwealth ignored the definition of "net income" and limited it to the net income actually received by a corporation during the calendar year. The court did not agree with the commonwealth's construction and held that (1) the commonwealth could not be estopped by the public statements or official acts of some of its highest officials; (2) 1947 Pa. Laws 232, if retroactively applied to net income from before the date of the statute's enactment, clearly violated both the federal and state constitutions; (3) the statute had to be strictly construed against the commonwealth and all reasonable doubts had to be resolved in favor of the taxpayers; and (4) by its terms and in its operation and effect, the statute arbitrarily and unreasonably discriminated against corporate taxpayers and therefore violated the Uniformity Clause of the Pennsylvania Constitution and the Fourteenth Amendment of the federal Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments in favor of the taxpayers.

 

429 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Delaware County Nat'l Bank v. Campbell


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


378 Pa. 311; 106 A.2d 416; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 597


Argued June 1, 1954  
June 28, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 34, May T., 1954, from order of Banking Board of Pennsylvania dated February 4, 1954, in case of Delaware County National Bank v. L. Merle Campbell, Secretary of Banking of Pennsylvania et al. Order affirmed.

Appeal in the nature of certiorari to review decision of Banking Board of Pennsylvania approving merger of banks.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Pennsylvania Banking Board dated February 4, 1954 is affirmed; each party to pay its respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national bank challenged the decision of the Banking Board of Pennsylvania (board) that approved the merger of two other banks arguing that the board approved the merger in error. Appellee, Secretary of Banking of Pennsylvania (secretary), brought motions to quash the appeal arguing that the decision was not subject to judicial review and that the national bank lacked standing to contest the merger.


OVERVIEW: The court dismissed the motions to quash and affirmed the order approving the merger. The court reviewed various sections of the Banking Code, 7 P.S. § 819 et seq., and the Department of Banking Code, 71 P.S. 733 et seq., and found no provision in either that prohibited judicial review of the merger order of the board. The court explained that when a statute was silent with respect to whether judicial review was available for an administrative decision, a judicial decision substantially affecting property rights, as was the order in this case, was reviewable. The court concluded that the national bank, because its main office and two of its branches were located in the same county as one of the merging banks and no other banks existed in that county, had standing to contest the merger. The court explained that the national bank had a direct interest in the subject matter and that its interest was immediate, pecuniary and substantial. The court interpreted § 204D of the Banking Code to permit the approval of a merger if the community in which the branch was to be established was without adequate banking facilities excluding the institutions that were parties to the proposed merger.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the motions to quash and affirmed the order approving the merger.

Sterling v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


378 Pa. 538; 106 A.2d 793; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 616


Argued April 21, 1954

OVERVIEW: The issues presented in the appeal were whether an ordinance of the city that imposed a so-called mercantile license tax included in its coverage members of the bar engaged in the practice of their profession, and if so, whether the ordinance was unconstitutional as an interference with the judicial branch of government. 431 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Weaverland Independent School Dist.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


378 Pa. 449; 106 A.2d 812; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 610


Argued April 19, 1954  
June 28, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 272, Jan. T., 1953, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, Trust Book 38, page 82, in re Weaverland Independent School District. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition of taxpayers for creation of independent school district. Before SCHAEFFER, P.J. and WISSLER, J.

Order entered dismissing petition, opinion by WISSLER, J. Petitioner appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order dismissing the petition is affirmed at the appellant's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania) dismissing her petition for the creation of an independent school district.


OVERVIEW: A majority of the taxable inhabitants of a specifically described contiguous territory located entirely within an existing school district petitioned the court of common pleas for the establishment of the described area as an independent school district. No answer was filed, but on the day scheduled for a hearing on the petition, the directors of the existing school district and the then projected school authority appeared in opposition to the establishment of the independent school district. After hearing testimony, the court of common pleas found that the creation of the proposed independent school district would be detrimental to the rest of the school district. On appeal, the court affirmed. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 24, § 242 specified that the superintendent of public instruction had final approval over the creation of new school districts. Since the superintendent voiced his disapproval, the district could not be created. Section 242 was constitutional because the legislature could make a law to delegate a power to determine some fact or state of things upon which the law made, or intended to make, its own action depend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the petition.

Habeas corpus. Before LEVINTHAL, J.

Order entered denying writ. Relator appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The relator sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus against the superintendent, county prison, and the State of Georgia.


OVERVIEW: The relator was arrested in Philadelphia on a charge of illegal flight from imprisonment in Georgia. The Governor of Pennsylvania issued a warrant for the relator's rendition to Georgia. The relator filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus that alleged that he had been subjected to cruel and unusual punishment while he was imprisoned in Georgia and that if he were returned to Georgia, the unlawful punishment would continue. The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied the relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus because the U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 2 provided for extradition upon demand, and the trial court was required to assume that a demanding state had no other object that to enforce its laws. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied the relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

433 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Duquesne Light Co. v. Upper St. Clair Tp.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


377 Pa. 323; 105 A.2d 287; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 517


Argued April 21, 1954  
May 24, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 171 and 173, March T., 1954, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1954, No. 1917, in case of Duquesne Light Company v. Township of Upper St. Clair et al. Decree affirmed; reargument refused June 4, 1954.

Bill in equity. Before SOFFEL, J.

Adjudication filed awarding plaintiff preliminary injunction. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree is affirmed, the costs of this appeal to be paid equally by the township and the Duquesne Light Company.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Upper St. Clair Township (township) sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted plaintiff utility's request for an injunction preventing the township from enforcing a zoning ordinance against the utility.


OVERVIEW: The utility sought condemnation of rights-of-way and easements on properties within the townships. The landowners protested the condemnations, and cited the utility's failure to comply with one of the township's zoning ordinances as a reason to deny the condemnation. The utility sought an injunction preventing the township from enforcing the zoning ordinance. The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting the injunction. The court held that the utility was not subject to the zoning ordinance because the zoning ordinance could not modify the Public Utility Code. The zoning ordinance did not expressly or impliedly grant zoning power with respect to uses and structures, other than buildings, of a utility company. The commonwealth did not delegate any power to townships to regulate utilities. The equity court was able to decide the zoning issue because the exhaustion doctrine was not applied to a legal remedy if the legal remedy was not adequate and complete or if its pursuit would have worked irreparable harm. Without immediate intervention, the utility would have been forced to curtail services to its customers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the utility's request for an injunction preventing the township from enforcing a zoning ordinance against the utility.

 

434 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Watson Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


377 Pa. 495; 105 A.2d 576; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 540


Argued April 1, 1954  
May 24, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 172, March T., 1952, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1951, No. 1492, in Appeal of Catherine L. Watson. Order affirmed; reargument refused June 19, 1954.

Appeal by appellant from decision of Superintendent of Public Instruction dismissing appellant as teacher. Before WEISS, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal. Appellant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed at the costs of the appellee School District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former teacher sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the decision of the Superintendent of Public Instruction ruling that the teacher's contract of employment was validly terminated for mental derangement by the Board of Directors of appellee School District of the City of McKeesport.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was dismissed on the ground that she suffered from mental derangement within the meaning of § 1122 of the Public School Code of 1949, P.L. 30, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 24, § 11-1122. The teacher complained that the Public School Code unconstitutionally deprived her of the right to a trial by jury on the issue of mental derangement since such right existed in Pennsylvania prior to the adoption of the Pennsylvania Constitution of 1874. She claimed that it was vouchsafed to her by Pa. Const. art. I, § 6, which provided that trial by jury would be as heretofore, and the right thereof would remain inviolate. The court disagreed and upheld the dismissal. The court held that no statute enacted prior to the Pennsylvania Constitution of 1874 entitled a teacher discharged for mental derangement to a trial of the issue by a jury. The Constitutional mandate had no applicability when the right did not previously exist. Since the teacher failed to show any prior right in a teacher dismissed because of mental derangement to a jury trial of the charge, it followed that the Public School Code did not deprive her of any constitutional right in respect of her dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Clark v. Meade


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


377 Pa. 150; 104 A.2d 465; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 501


Argued January 13, 1954  
March 29, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 90 and 91, Jan. T., 1954, from judgments of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1953, Nos. 9084 and 9034, in cases of Joseph S. Clark, Jr., Mayor, et al. v. William F. Meade et al., and Thomas P. McHenry et al. v. Joseph S. Clark, Jr., et al. Judgments reversed; reargument refused April 15, 1954.

Proceedings upon complaint in mandamus and upon petition for declaratory judgment.

Judgments entered dismissing complaint in action of mandamus and in favor of plaintiffs in declaratory judgment proceeding, before MacNEILLE, P.J., MILNER and WATERS, JJ., opinion by MILNER, J. Plaintiffs in action of mandamus, and defendants in declaratory judgment proceeding, appealed.



DISPOSITION: In No. 90 January Term, 1954, the dismissal of the complaint in mandamus is reversed; and there being no facts in dispute, the court below is directed to enter judgment in favor of the appellants, at the cost of the appellees.

In No. 91 January Term, 1954, the judgment of the court below is reversed and is here entered in favor of the appellants, at the cost of the appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mayor appealed from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition for a writ of mandamus. Defendants city sheriff, city commissioners, and members of the city board of revision of taxes appealed from the judgment of the trial court in favor of plaintiff in his declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: A state constitutional amendment, the Philadelphia Home-Rule Charter, abolished county government in the city of Philadelphia, providing the city with all previous duties and functions of county government, and making all county officers the officers of the city. A later constitutional enactment sought to bring certain offices, among them the offices of the sheriff, city commissioners, and members of the city board of tax revisions, outside the restrictions of the home-rule charter amendment, in particular those preventing those officers from engaging in political activities. The court held that the enactment was unconstitutional in that it violated the constitutional amendment providing for city home rule insofar as the charter amendment prohibited local laws which granted any individual any special or exclusive privilege or immunity. The court held the latest enactment to be a local law because it applied exclusively to the city of Philadelphia. The court concluded that there was no rational, substantial ground for the change in classification of the particular offices which the later enactment attempted to place beyond the reach of the restriction on political activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the complaint in mandamus, and directed the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the mayor.
