Medinger Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


377 Pa. 217; 104 A.2d 118; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 503


Argued January 6, 1954  
March 24, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No, 22, Jan. T., 1954, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Feb. T., 1952, No. 5, in Appeal of Russell L. Medinger et ux., from Zoning Board of Adjustment of Springfield Township. Order affirmed.

Appeal by property owners from decision of zoning board of adjustment refusing application for variance.

Order entered sustaining appeal and directing issuance of permit, opinion by KNIGHT, P.J. Township appealed.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Court below is affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township zoning board sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the appeal of respondent property owners, who challenged the denial of their application for a building permit for a home that did not meet the minimum habitable floor space specified by the township's zoning ordinance on a sliding scale that differed from one township district to another.


OVERVIEW: The property owners retained an architect to design a home for them that was a reproduction of an early farmhouse, and spent many years collecting the authentic building materials required. In time they applied for a building permit, which was refused. The property owners appealed to the Board of Adjustment (BOA), which dismissed their petition. The property owners then sought review before the common pleas court, which reversed the BOA, held the zoning ordinance unconstitutional, and directed that the permit be issued. The zoning board appealed. The court affirmed. The court found that the township was divided into different districts, and that the zoning ordinance prescribed a minimum habitable floor area that was different in each district. The home designed for the property owners was smaller than the minimum specified for their district, but was larger than the minimum prescribed in other districts. The court held that the ordinance could not be sustained on the grounds that it served to protect the health, safety, or morals of the citizens. The court held further that a zoning ordinance could not deprive property owners of their property solely for aesthetic purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that sustained the appeal of the property owners who challenged the denial of a building permit for a home that did not meet the minimum habitable floor space prescribed by the township's zoning regulation for the district in which the property owners proposed to build their home, although the home would meet the habitable floor space requirement of other of the township's districts.

The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania

Loomis v. Board of Education


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


376 Pa. 428; 103 A.2d 769; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 460


Argued November 20, 1953  
March 22, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 342, Jan. T., 1953, from judgment of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1953, No. 33, affirming judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1951, No. 2346, in case of Paul A. Loomis v. The Board of Education of School District of Philadelphia. Judgment affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 173 Pa. Super. Ct. 597.

Assumpsit.

Defendant's preliminary objections to complaint dismissed and judgment entered for plaintiff for want of an answer, opinion of LEVINTHAL, J. Defendant appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the judgment of the court below. Appeal by defendant to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Superior Court sustaining the action of the lower court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Philadelphia School District Board of Education (board) challenged the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) judgment affirming a decision in favor of plaintiff teacher in an action in assumpsit under 65 P.S. § 114 (1935) seeking to recover back pay for periods during which he served as a reservist in the United States Army. The board asserted that § 114 was unconstitutional special legislation that violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 7, 8.


OVERVIEW: The teacher initiated an action in assumpsit under 65 P.S. § 114 (1935) against the board seeking to recover back pay for periods during which he served as a reservist in the United States Army. The board filed preliminary objections on the ground that § 114 was unconstitutional special legislation in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 7, 8. The trial court dismissed the objections and rendered judgment for the teacher. The appellate court affirmed and the board appealed. The court affirmed holding that the test of class legislation was its reasonableness. It concluded that military leave of absence for 15 days with full pay was analogous to sick leave without loss of pay as an incident or condition of employment. While such leaves would have been offensive to the constitution if they were granted to special classes of employees with no reciprocal benefit to the state, the 15-day leave of absence granted to reservists was reasonable. Further, the military leave conferred a benefit upon the public employer and taxpayer in the quality of service rendered and was in the interest of national defense. The public derived benefit from it and this justified the classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court sustaining the judgment of the trial court in favor of the teacher in his action in assumpsit against the board seeking compensation for the time that he was on military leave as a reservist in the United States Army.

Fitzgerald v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


376 Pa. 379; 102 A.2d 887; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 455


Argued January 12, 1954  
February 10, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 283, Jan. T., 1953, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County, Sept T., 1952, No. 6212, in case of Marie S. Fitzgerald v. City of Philadelphia et al. Judgment affirmed; reargument refused March 4, 1954.

Mandamus proceeding.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and judgment entered for defendants, before BOK, P.J., FLOOD and LEVINTHAL, JJ., opinion by BOK, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 6 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which refused to reinstate her to her position as a nurse in a state hospital after she was dismissed for refusing to take the loyalty oath required by the Pennsylvania Loyalty Act, 1951 Pa. Laws. 1726.


OVERVIEW: The employee refused to take the loyalty oath required by the Pennsylvania Loyalty Act, 1951 Pa. Laws. 1726, and was dismissed from her position as a nurse in a state hospital. The Civil Service Commission denied her appeal and the lower court refused to reinstate her. The court affirmed. The court found that the oath was justified for the purpose of informing the appointing authority whether an employee was a member of a subversive organization and therefore not a fit person to be employed by the government. The court concluded that the oath was not unduly vague because it proscribed membership in an organization known by the employee to be subversive and did not punish honest ignorance. Although the oath did infringe upon the rights granted by U.S. Const. amend. I, the court held that the limitation of personal freedoms was justified to further an overriding public interest. Lastly, the court held that the legislature did not act arbitrarily in extending the oath requirement to all public employees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment refusing to reinstate the employee to her position as a nurse in a state hospital after she was dismissed for refusing to take a loyalty oath.

 

440 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Nelson


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


377 Pa. 58; 104 A.2d 133; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 497


Argued May 27, 1953  
January 25, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 94, March T., 1953, from judgment of Superior Court, April T., 1952, No. 170, affirming judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Allegheny County, Oct. Sessions, 1950, No. 764, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Steve Nelson, Judgment reversed; reargument refused April 27, 1954.

Same case in Superior Court: 172 Pa. Super. Ct. 125.

Indictment charging defendant with violations of § 207 of the Act of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872. Before MONTGOMERY, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence thereon. Defendant appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the judgment of the court below. Appeal by defendant to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the indictment quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed his conviction for attempting to overthrow the government of the United States by force and violence in violation of § 207 of the Pennsylvania Sedition Act, 18 P.S. § 4207. The trial court sentenced defendant to a 20-year prison term.


OVERVIEW: Because of defendant's involvement with the Communist Party, he was charged and convicted of attempting to overthrow the government of the United States by force and violence. The trial court denied defendant's motions for a new trial and in arrest of judgment. After the appellate court affirmed his conviction, defendant sought review. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction and quashed the indictment. The court held that the Pennsylvania Sedition Act was suspended by operation of law upon the enactment by Congress of the Smith Act, 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2384-2385, which defined sedition against the United States and prescribed the punishment therefor. Because the Pennsylvania Sedition Act was superseded, the court ruled that defendant's conviction was not sustained. The court stated that where federal legislation touched a field in which the federal interest was so dominant, U.S. Const. art. IV precluded enforcement of state laws on the same subject. The court concluded that the state punishment of sedition against the United States intruded into a matter of national interest and that the federal government exclusively controlled the field.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for attempting to overthrow the government of the United States by force and violence and quashed the indictment.

 

441 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Butler County Nat'l Bank


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


376 Pa. 66; 101 A.2d 699; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 413


Argued October 6, 1953  
January 12, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 6, May T., 1954, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1947, Commonwealth Docket No. 113, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. The Butler County National Bank. Judgment affirmed.

Appeal by defendant from decision of Board of Finance and Review refusing to review settlement for tax on value of shares of capital stock. Before SOHN, J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed finding for Commonwealth; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and judgment entered for plaintiff. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bank sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed exceptions to adjudication from the Board of Finance and Review refusing to review settlement for tax on value of shares of capital stock in an action involving plaintiff Commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: The question presented was whether unrealized appreciation on securities held for investment purposes should be used in determining the actual value of the capital shares of banks for taxation purposes under the provisions of Pa. Act of July 15, 1897, P.L. 292, as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 1931. The question was answered in the affirmative by the trial court. The $ 685,575 at issue was the difference between the aggregate cost of the securities, as reflected by the books of the bank, and the aggregate market value of the same securities. The court held that the bank used the most approved accounting practices in carrying on its books its investment securities at cost. However, the appraisal of such investments at their market value contributed to a more truly actual valuation of the bank's capital shares. Sound corporate accounting practices were not designed to show the actual worth of a bank's shares but rather their rock-bottom value, in short, the most conservative estimate possible. The value had to reflect the actual value of assets on that date as determined from facts and based upon reasonable indicia of their material worth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

442 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


O. H. Martin Co. v. Sharpsburg


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


376 Pa. 242; 102 A.2d 125; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 437


Argued October 9, 1953  
January 11, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 177, March T., 1953, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1952, No. 1803, in case of O.H. Martin Company v. Borough of Sharpsburg, Dennis J. Casper, Burgess, and Catherine M. Cavanaugh, Tax Collector. Decree reversed.

Bill in equity. Before NIXON, J.

Adjudication filed finding tax ordinance unconstitutional; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered awarding plaintiff injunctive relief. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and bill dismissed at cost of appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borough sought review from a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that was entered in favor of plaintiff, a Pennsylvania corporation engaged in building construction and general contracting, in an action to enjoin the borough from enforcement of an ordinance under which it taxed gross receipts of individuals or corporation offering service to the general public within the borough.


OVERVIEW: The corporation contended that the ordinance did not distinguish between interstate and intrastate commerce, and that this defect was not cured by the savings clause, it contained no formula for apportionment between receipts from interstate and intrastate commerce, and it unlawfully delegated to the tax collector the authority to determine who was required to pay the tax. The trial court held that the ordinance was invalid because there was no formula for apportionment of receipts, and that it unlawfully delegated the administration and enforcement to the tax collector. The court held that a direct State tax upon the privilege of conducting interstate commerce was invalid. However, merely because a portion of the receipts of a business was derived from interstate transactions did not preclude assessment and collection of a tax on its intrastate activities. The court held that the receipts from intrastate business were separable from its interstate receipts, and the omission from the ordinance of a formula for apportionment did not render it valid. The court further held that improper delegation of legislative authority to the tax collector did not render the ordinance invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree and dismissed the bill.

 

443 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Gambone v. Commonwealth


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


375 Pa. 547; 101 A.2d 634; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 385


Argued November 18, 1953  
January 4, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 11, May T., 1954, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1951, Equity Docket, No. 2004 and Commonwealth Docket, No. 247, in case of Charles Gambone and Charles S. Gambone, trading as Gambones' Atlantic Service Station v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al. Decree affirmed.

Bill in equity. Before SOHN, J.

Adjudication filed finding Act of September 28, 1951, P.L. 1548 unconstitutional; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final order entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, sought review of a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which sustained a bill in equity by plaintiff gasoline dealers. The gasoline dealers alleged that Pa. Act of September 28, 1951, Pa. P.L. 1548, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly concluded that the prohibition of the posting on the gasoline dealers' premises or adjacent property of price signs in excess of a certain prescribed size was unreasonable and arbitrary and bore no rational relation to public health, safety, morals, or welfare. The size of the sign would not have any relevancy to the perpetration of fraud. On the contrary, the larger the sign the more difficult it would be for the gasoline dealers to deceive a purchaser. The prohibition in Pa. Penal Code of June 24, 1939, Pa. P.L. 872, § 857, already directed against the placing of any false statements concerning the price. Price cutting was not really an evil. Since there was nothing in law to prevent the gasoline dealers from selling the gasoline at any price they chose, there was no reason why the gasoline dealers should not be allowed to advertise such price. The denial of that right was a taking of property without due process. The court held that that Pa. Act of September 28, 1951, Pa. P.L. 1548, violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 1 and 9 and U.S. Const. amend. 14. Therefore, the court held that the Act was null and void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree.

 

444 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pincus v. Power


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


376 Pa. 175; 101 A.2d 914; 1954 Pa. LEXIS 427


Argued November 16, 1953  
January 4, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 240, Jan. T., 1953, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1952, No. 6508, in case of Jacob M. Pincus and Nathan Pincus v. John E. Powers, Jr., et al., constituting the Zoning Board of Adjustment and Chelten Hills Civic League. Order affirmed; reargument refused January 27, 1954.

Appeal by applicants from decision of Zoning Board of Adjustment refusing variance certificates and use registration permits. Before SMITH, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding against applicants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final order entered. Applicants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas is affirmed; costs to be paid by Appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicants sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an action of defendant, zoning board of adjustment. The board refused to grant variance certificates and use registration permits to the applicants.


OVERVIEW: The applicants wanted to erect six two-story structures on their property. The ground floor of each structure was to be used for a variety of commercial retail stores. The second floor of each structure was to be used as an apartment for a single-family dwelling. A city counsel refused to change the zoning of the block where the applicants' property was located. The board found that the safety, health, and general welfare of the immediate neighborhood would be affected to its detriment if the variance were granted. The trial court pointed out that there must be a line of demarcation between commercial stores and residential properties. The fact that the applicants could sell their land at a far higher price if the zoning was changed or if the variance was granted was not an unnecessary hardship or a sufficient reason to grant the variance. Since the only substantial hardship was that the applicants' property would be more valuable if the variance was granted, the court agreed with the board and the trial court that this alone did not constitute an unnecessary hardship. Adequate evidence supported the findings of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court ordered the applicants to pay costs.

 

445 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Shirks Motor Exp. Corp. v. Messner


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


375 Pa. 450; 100 A.2d 913; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 480


Argued April 20, 1953  
November 17, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 22 and 25, May T., 1953, from decrees of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1952, Equity Docket, Nos. 2015 and 2024, Commonwealth Docket Nos. 34 and 94, in cases of Shirks Motor Express Corporation v. Otto F. Messner, Secretary, Department of Revenue and Weldon B. Heyburn, Auditor General, and Interstate Motor Freight System, Inc. v. Same. Decrees affirmed; reargument refused December 30, 1953.

Bills in equity.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and decrees entered dismissing bills, opinions by NEELEY, J. Plaintiffs, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decrees of the court below which dismissed the complaint in each of these two cases are affirmed at the cost of the respective appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant carriers challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed cases challenging an action by appellees, Secretary of the Department of Revenue and Auditor General, enforcing 72 P.S. § 2185 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The carriers filed separate bills in equity against appellees to enjoin them from enforcing an act which imposed an excise tax on the gross receipts of common carriers by motor vehicle. Appellees filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer, which in each case were sustained, and the respective complaints dismissed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgments. The court held the statute provided a reasonably accurate and nondiscriminatory formula to reflect the use of highways within Pennsylvania. The burden of proving that the tax was unreasonable was on the carrier and it failed to carry that burden. The fact that one carrier or other marginal truck carriers would operate at a loss if the tax was applied did not establish that the tax was unreasonable. The carrier did not show that the tax plus the toll exceeded fair compensation for its use of the turnpike. Even though the nature and amount of the increase in the tax could not have been anticipated, the retroactive effect of an amendment did not constitute a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court dismissing the carriers' challenge of an excise tax on the gross receipts of common carriers applied by appellees was affirmed.

 

446 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Otto Milk Co. v. Rose


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


375 Pa. 18; 99 A.2d 467; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 433


Argued March 23, 1953  
October 5, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 48, March T., 1953, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County, June T., 1950, No. 355, in case of Otto Milk Company v. Walter E. Rose, Mayor of City of Johnstown, et al. Judgment reversed.

Mandamus. Before McCANN, P.J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed finding for defendants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and judgment entered for defendants. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed at the cost of appellees. The record is remanded to the court below with direction to issue a writ of mandamus to compel defendants to grant to plaintiff the permit applied for, either forthwith, or, at the option of defendants, after such reasonable inspections, if any, of plaintiff's dairy farms, receiving stations and pasteurization plants, as defendants may choose to make, and upon their finding therefrom that the production, care and treatment of plaintiff's milk sufficiently comply with the sanitary regulations provided in the city's applicable ordinance and those of the city's Department of Health.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff milk company sought review of a judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of defendants, the City of Johnstown and certain of its officials, in the milk distributor's mandamus action to compel defendants to issue it a permit to sell milk within the City of Johnstown.


OVERVIEW: The milk company, which distributed milk wholesale in paper containers, had been in business for some 25 years, had an unblemished record with regard to sanitation in its plants and sources of supply, and had been licensed by the state milk control commission and the U.S. Department of Agriculture. It obtained its milk from nearly 800 farms, some of which were up to 200 miles away from the city. The city responded to its request for a permit by passing an ordinance requiring an examination of every place handling the company's milk, with delivered raw or pasteurized to the consumer, and another ordinance disallowing any inspection of farms more than 50 miles distant. The court found that although the city was authorized to enact regulations to insure the purity and wholesomeness of milk as a condition to the granting of permission for its sale or distribution within its jurisdiction, such regulations had to be reasonable and not arbitrary and absolutely prohibitive. The court found that the city effectively told the milk company that it was inconvenient to inspect their farms and, therefore, denied it the right to sell the milk in violation of its constitutional right of property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered the record remanded to the trial court with directions to issue a writ of mandamus to compel defendants either to issue the requested permit forthwith or to issue the permit if sanitation standards were met after reasonable inspections of the dairy company's facilities had been conducted.

Commonwealth v. Mellon Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 519; 98 A.2d 168; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 419

Appeal by taxpayer from decision of Board of Finance and Review on capital stock tax assessment.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, had made a tax assessment on the capital stock of appellee national bank under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 1931. Upon the bank's appeal, the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) reduced the amount of the assessment. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The matter had come before the common pleas court on the bank's appeal from the settlement of its tax on outstanding shares of capital stock. The appeal was tried without a jury and resulted in a final order that directed the entry of a judgment for the Commonwealth for a significantly lower amount, with directions to the Commonwealth to refund or credit the bank the excess amount that it had paid. The question that the Commonwealth raised on appeal was whether the common pleas court had followed the proper formula, as indicated by statutory and decisional law, for determining the Pennsylvania tax liability of the bank. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the Pennsylvania tax on the bank was invalid because it violated U. S. Rev. Stat. § 5219 in that the tax that had been assessed against the bank had been at a greater rate than the tax on other moneyed capital in the hands of citizens of Pennsylvania that came into competition with the business of national banks.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Lancaster City Ordinance


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 529; 98 A.2d 25; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 420


Argued May 26, 1953  
June 26, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 113, Jan. T., 1953, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County, June Sessions, 1952, Minutes 549, in re Lancaster City Ordinance No. 16-1952. Order affirmed.

Appeal from annexation ordinance (No. 16-1952). Before SCHAEFER, P.J. and WISSLER, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal. Township Board of Commissioners, School District, Tax Collector, and an individual resident and taxpayer, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is accordingly affirmed, with costs on the appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, township officials and a resident taxpayer, sought review of an order by which the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania) dismissed their appeal by which they contested the validity of appellee city's annexation ordinance and proceedings. The township officials and resident claimed that the applicable enabling legislation violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 3 and 7.


OVERVIEW: The council of the city enacted Lancaster, Pa., Ordinance No. 16-1952, by which township land was annexed to the city. The township officials and resident challenged the ordinance and annexation proceedings, claiming that the enabling statutes, the Third Class City Law, Act of 1931, P.L. 932, and the Third Class City Code, Act of 1951, P.L. 662, violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 3 and 7. The township officials and resident argued that the titles to the Acts did not indicate that the Acts addressed annexation and that they prescribed different procedures and powers for annexation by cities of the third class than those prescribed for other cities. The trial court dismissed the appeal. On further review, the court affirmed. The court reasoned that the Third Class City Law and the Third Class City Code referred generally to powers of third class cities in their titles and were consolidations and reenactments of earlier laws, which referred to annexation in their titles. The court held that Pa. Const. art. III, § 34 allowed the classification of cities and provided that legislation applicable to a particular class was not special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re Lancaster City Ordinance


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 537; 98 A.2d 29; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 421


Argued May 26, 1953  
June 26, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 204, Jan. T., 1953, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County, Sept. Sessions, 1952, Minutes 558, in re Lancaster City Ordinance No. 33-1952. Order affirmed; reargument refused July 21, 1953.

Appeal from annexation ordinance (No. 33-1952). Before SCHAEFER, P.J., and WISSLER, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal. Township Board of Commissioners, School District, Tax Collector, and an individual resident and taxpayer, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the court below is affirmed, with costs on the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which validated Ordinance No. 33-1952, Pa., an annexation ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The Ordinance was enacted by the City of Lancaster, Pennsylvania, for the annexation of certain lands in Manheim Township, Pennsylvania. Because the property owners lived on the land in question, they contended in the trial court that their nonjoinder in the petition for annexation rendered the petition fatal. The property owners then petitioned to join nunc pro tunc in the annexation petition. The trial court allowed these proceedings, which the court agreed with. Beforehand, however, Manheim Township advanced from a second-class township to a first-class township rating, which the property owners contended invalidated the annexation. The court affirmed the order validating the annexation. The court found that the proceedings under consideration were initiated prior to the promotion to first class status. Rights had thus accrued to the taxable inhabitants of the territory annexed. Under the provisions of the Act of May 27, 1949, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 19092-108, those rights could not have been divested. As the passage of the Ordinance predated the change of Manheim Township's status, its validity remained unimpaired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

450 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Lancaster City Ordinance


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 546; 98 A.2d 34; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 424


Argued May 26, 1953  
June 26, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 203, Jan. T., 1953, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County, Sept. Sessions, 1952, Minutes 553 1/2, in re Lancaster City Ordinance No. 27-1952. Order reversed.

Appeal from annexation ordinance (No. 27-1952). Before SCHAEFER, P.J., and WISSLER, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal. Township Board of Commissioners, School District, Tax Collector, and an individual resident and taxpayer, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is reversed, with costs on appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a township board of commissioners, school district, and tax collector, and an individual taxpayer, sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the annexation of less than one acre in the township to appellee City of Lancaster by Lancaster, Pa., Ordinance No. 27-1952, as sought by appellee petitioning property owner. The lower court also dismissed the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The annexation area embraced only one-half of the width of a township road. As a result, the ordinance left between the annexed area and the City line two pieces of land, both under the township's jurisdiction. Appellants sought to determine whether township land was "contiguous" to and subject to annexation by the City when the land was separated from the existing City boundary by half the width of the bed of a township highway and when no part of the highway was included in the description of the tract to be annexed. The lower court answered yes. On appeal, the court reversed. It held that there was nothing in the Annexation Statute, which was the Pennsylvania Act of 1951, P.L. 662, § 5, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 52, § 12198-501, suggesting that contiguity meant anything other than contiguity. If the legislature intended to include in the annexable field land that was "nearby," it would have said so. The exact and authoritative location of municipal boundaries was imperative. The court suggested that the difficulties could have been avoided if the petition for annexation had been drawn to include the bed of the road, thus achieving a physical bondage between the two pieces of land.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, with the costs on appellees.

Commonwealth v. Hallberg


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 554; 97 A.2d 849; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 426


Argued January 14, 1953; reargued May 25, 1953  
June 26, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 15, March T., 1952, from judgment of Superior Court, April T., 1950, No. 172, affirming order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Somerset County, Sept. Sessions, 1950, No. 2, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Roy W. Hallberg. Judgment reversed.

Same case in Superior Court: 168 Pa. Super. Ct. 596.

Appeal by defendant from conviction before justice of the peace for violation of § 905 (a) of The Vehicle Code.

Defendant's motion to quash information sustained, opinion by LANSBERRY, P.J. Commonwealth appealed to the Superior Court, which affirmed the order of the court below. Appeal by Commonwealth to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Superior Court affirming the quashing of the information against the defendant is reversed, and the record is remanded to the Court of Quarter Sessions of Somerset County for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order that sustained defendant's motion to quash an information. Defendant was convicted before a justice of the peace of a violation of § 905(a) of Pa. Vehicle Code of May 1, 1929, P.L. 905.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving a motor vehicle that was too wide upon a highway without proper permits. Defendant argued that the amendment of § 905 of Pa. Vehicle Code of May 1, 1929, P.L. 905, by § 1 of Pa. Act of June 5, 1937, P.L. 1718, was an abrogation from the Vehicle Code because the amendment failed to include a penalty paragraph. The court disagreed and reversed the judgment sustaining defendant's motion to quash the information. The court stated that it was clear from § 71 of Pa. Statutory Construction Act of May 28, 1937, P.L. 1019 that, where the legislature intended to eliminate any section or part of a law, it was not enough merely to delete the publication of that section or part, but the entire section or part, including the section or part to be eliminated, must be published at length, with the section or part to be eliminated enclosed in brackets. Therefore, the court held that the attempted amendment of § 905 of Pa. Vehicle Code of May 1, 1929, P.L. 905, was invalid because it failed to comply with state constitutional and statutory requirements and, therefore, the entire section remained in force as it existed prior to the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment affirming the quashing of the information against defendant and the record was remanded to the Court of Quarter Sessions of Somerset County for further proceedings.

Koehnlein v. Retirement System for Employees


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


373 Pa. 535; 97 A.2d 88; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 343


Argued March 31, 1953  
May 25, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 77, March T., 1953, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Oct. T., 1952, No. 869, in case of Joseph Koehnlein v. Retirement System for the Employees of Allegheny County. Judgment reversed.

Proceeding upon petition of claimant for declaratory judgment.

Order entered granting prayer of petition, before ELLENBOGEN, SMART and NIXON, JJ., opinion by NIXON, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and is here entered for the defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Retirement System for the Employees of Allegheny County (county), appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) in favor of plaintiff retiree, in his action for declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of an amendment to the county's retirement system, 16 P.S. § 312, which was intended to increase retirement allowances payable to county employees after they had been retired.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the amendment to the system that was intended to increase the retirement allowance payable to a county employee after he retired was constitutional, and granted the claimant an increase in his retirement allotment. The county appealed, contending that the amendment violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 11, 18; Pa. Const. art. I, § 17. The court reversed because the trial court's decision was not a sound legal interpretation of what the retirement contract contemplated. The retirement allowance was fixed by 16 P.S. § 312 in terms of dollars and not purchasing power. There was nothing in the provisions governing the system to justify a retirement allowance based on earned compensation adjusted to a "cost of living" index or other standard related to buying power. Without some such provision, the amendment to 16 P.S. § 312 was unconstitutional because it legislatively augmented the pension of people already retired. The court thus held that the amendment violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 11 as to employees already retired at the time of the passage of the amendment and was, therefore, to that extent void and of no effect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and entered judgment for the county in the retiree's action for declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of the amendment.

Narehood v. Pearson


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


374 Pa. 299; 96 A.2d 895; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 397


Argued April 21, 1953  
May 25, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 197, Jan. T., 1953, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Clearfield County, Feb. T., 1953, in Equity, No 2, in case of Millard Narehood, et al., Taxpayers of Clearfield County, v. A. W. Pearson, et al., County Commissioners of Clearfield County, etc. Judgment reversed.

Bill in equity.

Order entered dismissing preliminary objections, opinion by BELL, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county commissioners appealed dismissal of their preliminary objections in the Court of Common Pleas of Clearfield County (Pennsylvania) where plaintiff taxpayers sought an injunction against the valuation and assessment of real property tax as illegal, unconstitutional, arbitrary, and discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: When assessments on real property increased by 400 percent, the taxpayers filed a bill in equity to enjoin the county commissioners and the board of assessment and revision of taxes from proceeding. They claimed that the assessments were illegal and unconstitutional because they were arbitrary and discriminatory. The lower court overruled and dismissed defendants' preliminary objections, and the county commissioners appealed. On review, the court held that the assessors could not, in just a few months, gather all the required data, information, cost charts and land values. It determined that if injustice resulted from irregularities in the assessments, it could be corrected on appeal. The court commented that the taxpayers had failed to realize the time involved and practical difficulties that confronted the assessors. The classification of land into surface, mineral, and farmland was not arbitrary, discriminatory or illegal, but was reasonable, practical and just; it did not violate any constitutional provision. In reversing, the court held that defendants' preliminary objections should have been sustained, and the amended bill of complaint should have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, holding that defendants' preliminary objections should have been sustained, and the taxpayers' amended complaint should have been dismissed.

 

454 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Hatton v. Dye


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


373 Pa. 502; 96 A.2d 127; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 337


Argued March 31, 1953  
April 22, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 50, March T., 1953, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1952, No. 2016, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Everett Hatton v. Charles Dye, Warden, Allegheny County Jail. Order reversed.

Habeas corpus. Before ELLENBOGEN, J.

Order entered granting writ and directing relator be discharged in extradition proceeding. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is reversed and it is directed that the relator be delivered to the Mississippi authorities in accordance with the requisition for extradition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted relator's writ of habeas corpus and directed that he be discharged in an extradition proceeding.


OVERVIEW: At the age of 17, relator was convicted in Mississippi of assault with intent to rape and sentenced to life in prison. He escaped and settled in Pennsylvania, where he married. About 22 years after his conviction, relator was arrested in Pennsylvania and discovered to be a fugitive from justice. A request for extradition was made, issued, and executed. Relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was granted. On review, the court reversed the trial court's order and directed relator delivered to Mississippi authorities. The trial court exceeded the scope of permissible inquiry on a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in an extradition proceeding. Section 20 of the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, P.L. 288, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 191 et seq., prohibited inquiry into the guilt or innocence of the accused. A showing of a conviction, sentence, commitment, and escape were sufficient for the purpose of extradition. Because there was no question of relator's arrest in Pennsylvania, his identity, his presence in Mississippi at the time the crime was committed, or the proper execution of the extradition papers, the trial court had no jurisdiction to inquire further into the matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and directed that the relator be delivered to the Mississippi authorities in accordance with the requisition for extradition.

Crane v. Crane


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


373 Pa. 1; 95 A.2d 199; 1953 Pa. LEXIS 277


Argued January 9, 1953  
February 13, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 21, March T., 1953, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Armstrong County, June T., 1952, No. 297, in case of Jean M. Crane v. Radford R. Crane and Eljer Company. Order affirmed; reargument refused March 24, 1953.

Bill in equity.

Defendant corporation's petition under the Act of 1925 questioning the jurisdiction of the court dismissed, opinion by BRAHAM, P.J., specially presiding. Defendant corporation appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Armstrong County (Pennsylvania), which refused to dismiss an action by plaintiff wife. The wife brought an action for an injunction against the company and maintenance from defendant husband, who did not appeal. The trial court directed the company to answer the averments of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The company alleged that shares of the company's stock were not property such as to confer jurisdiction upon the trial court. No effective transfer of the certificates of the stock could be made without the wife's joinder. Therefore, the purpose of the Uniform Transfer Act, Pa. Act of May 5, 1911, P.L. 126, was not affected. The court held that the Act was inapplicable. As far as the declared, but unpaid, dividends on the stock of the company were concerned, the dividends constituted a debt of the company and as such had a situs for proceedings in the nature of a foreign attachment. The husband had an interest in all property owned as tenants by the entireties. There was no reason why that interest should not be applied to the support of the wife whom the husband had deserted. Accordingly, after the trial court made an order for the wife's maintenance, the order might be implemented by proceedings to enable her to enforce it by liquidation of the shares of stock and the accumulated dividends thereon owned by them as tenants by the entireties. This would enable the wife to obtain satisfaction out of her husband's interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Francis v. Neville Tp.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


372 Pa. 77; 92 A.2d 892; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 471


Argued September 29, 1952  
December 6, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 195, March T., 1952, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1952, No. 883, in case of Cledwyn D. Francis v. The Township of Neville, Board of Commissioners of the Township of Neville, John Barna, Jr., Secretary, and Donald S. Ferguson, Treasurer. Order affirmed.

Mandamus.

Defendants' preliminary objections sustained and order entered dismissing complaint, before SOFFEL, MONTGOMERY and THOMPSON, JJ., opinion by THOMPSON, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order sustaining the defendants' preliminary objections and dismissing the plaintiff's complaint is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained appellee township's preliminary objections and dismissed the employee's complaint. The employee had filed suit to obtain a writ of mandamus to compel the township to make pension payments to him.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the township for 28 years. The employee was promised that he would receive a monthly pension so long as he should live, and this assurance was conveyed through the passage of Neville Township, Pa., Ordinance No. 361. The succeeding board of commissioners repealed the ordinance. The township secretary therefore refused to make pension payments to the employee, and the employee instituted a mandamus proceeding. The common pleas court sustained the township's preliminary objections and dismissed the complaint. The employee appealed. In affirming, the court held that Neville Township, Pa., Ordinance No. 361 was void and ineffective. The court reasoned that the ordinance violated § 605 of the Act of May 27, 1949, P.L. 1955, § 18, p. 1981 (Pennsylvania) because it did not set up a pension system for employees, but for one employee. For that same reason, the ordinance also violated Pa. Const. art. IX, § 7, and Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 7, 11, 18. The court also held that the employee had no vested right to the pension because no vested right could be founded on an ordinance which had no constitutional authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

In re Albert Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


372 Pa. 13; 92 A.2d 663; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 466


Argued September 30, 1952  
November 25, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 77, March T., 1952, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1951, No. 1689, in Appeal of Dorothy Albert from the decision, order and ruling of Dr. Francis B. Haas, Superintendent of Public Instruction. Decree affirmed.

Appeal by teacher from dismissal by Board of Public Education.

Appeal dismissed and final order entered, opinion by ELLENBOGEN, J., concurring opinion by NIXON, J. Teacher appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below dismissing the appeal of Dorothy Albert from the order of the Superintendent of Public Instruction is affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee board of public education dismissed appellant teacher for advocating or participating in un-American or subversive doctrines in violation of § 1122 of the School Code. The teacher challenged the decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the order of the superintendent of public instruction upholding the board's decision and dismissed her appeal.


OVERVIEW: The board dismissed the teacher, a Communist, for violating § 1122 by advocating or participating in un-American or subversive doctrines. The superintendent sustained the board's action; the trial court affirmed the superintendent's order and dismissed her appeal. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the use of the words "un-American or subversive doctrines" in § 1122 was not so ambiguous or obscure as to render the provision unconstitutionally vague. The words' connotation was no more uncertain than other dismissal causes enumerated in the same section and upheld by the courts. The court found that the legislature had the right to prescribe qualifications for public school teachers in terms of their moral characters and their loyalty to the state and federal governments because it was essential to protect the children from treacherous influences. The court ruled that, because the teacher failed to request a hearing de novo in the trial court in order to present evidence showing that the Communist Party was not a subversive organization, she could not complain on appeal that she was denied due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which had dismissed the teacher's appeal from the superintendent's order affirming her discharge. The court ordered the teacher to pay the costs.

 

458 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Cox's, Inc. v. Snodgrass


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


372 Pa. 148; 92 A.2d 540; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 479


Argued October 8, 1952  
November 25, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 213, March T., 1952, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Jan. T., 1949, No. 2798, in case of Cox's Incorporated v. W. Homer Snodgrass et ux., Milnor P. Clark, Margaret Electa Clark, Effie Minerva Clark and William L. Buck. Judgment reversed.

Bill in equity to quiet title. Before MUSMANNO, J.

Verdict directed for plaintiff and judgment entered thereon. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and here entered for the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which directed a verdict for appellee landowner and entered judgment thereon in appellee's action in equity to quiet title.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance providing that an alley, which abutted appellee's land and over which it was necessary to traverse to reach appellants' land, be vacated. Appellee alleged that the alley appeared on the municipal plan before it appeared as part of a plan of lots from which lots were sold to appellants' predecessor in title, that the original grantees took title with knowledge that the alley was part of the city's plan, and that the effect of the city's ordinance was to extinguish all public and private rights to use the alley. Appellants alleged that the original owner of the land had laid out a plan of lots, including the alley, prior to the time the alley appeared on any municipal plan, that the deed to appellee was expressly made subject to all outstanding rights, and that the board of viewers' proceeding did not extinguish appellants' easement. The court reversed because appellee failed to prove that the alley was a part of the city's municipal plan before it was plotted as part of a plan of lots by a grantor in appellants' chain of title or that the city intended to condemn private rights in the alley while terminating public rights and duties therein.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee in its action to quiet title and entered judgment for appellants.

 

459 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Olan Mills, Inc. v. Sharon


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


371 Pa. 609; 92 A.2d 222; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 456


Argued October 2, 1952  
November 18, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 138, March T., 1952, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County, Sept. T., 1950, in Equity, No. 3, in case of Olan Mills, Inc. v. City of Sharon, Myron W. Jones, Mayor, and William E. Stuart, Chief of Police. Decree reversed.

Bill in equity. Before ROWLEY, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding ordinance valid and directing dismissal of bill; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below dismissing the bill in equity is reversed and the record remanded for the entry of an appropriate order granting the injunction. Costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant photographic studio sought to overturn a decree of the Common Pleas Court of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed its bill that sought to enjoin the enforcement of Sharon, Pa., Ordinance 410. Appellee city opposed the studio's challenge to the ordinance, which regulated transient businesses.


OVERVIEW: The studio leased premises in the city for one and two-thirds months so that it could engage in the photography business. However, it did not pay the $ 200 per month license fee that the city contended that the studio was required to pay. Thus, an employee of the studio was arrested for violating Ordinance 410, and the studio filed its bill seeking to enjoin the enforcement of the ordinance. However, the ordinance did not contain any regulatory provisions. The trial court included the costs of litigation in reaching its conclusion that the ordinance was enforceable and in deciding not to enjoin its enforcement. The court reversed the trial court's decree, holding that the license fee was excessive because it greatly exceeded the cost of enforcing the ordinance. The court ruled that an assessment of taxes for revenue purposes was not an exercise of police power; thus, because the license fee was excessive, it was a tax, and the fee could not be sustained on police power grounds. The court also ruled that the costs of litigation could not be considered in determining the reasonableness of the fee because to do so was tantamount to requiring the studio to pay the city's counsel fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

Sablosky v. Messner


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


372 Pa. 47; 92 A.2d 411; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 467


Argued October 3, 1952  
November 18, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 4, May T., 1953, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1952, Commonwealth Docket No. 14, Equity Docket No. 2011, in case of Lewis Sablosky et al., trading as Norris Amusement Company and Lawrence Tornetta v. Otto F. Messner, Secretary of Revenue. Judgment affirmed.

Bill in equity.

Adjudication filed finding Act constitutional; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final judgment entered for defendant, opinion by RICHARDS, P.J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed at cost of appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) upheld the constitutionality of the Realty Transfer Tax Act (act), 1951 Pa. Laws 1742, in an action by plaintiffs, the sellers and purchaser of certain land, challenging its constitutionality. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, plaintiffs argued that § 3 of the act was unconstitutional because it was vague and uncertain as to whether the buyer or the seller, or both, were responsible for the tax imposed. Plaintiffs also argued that the definition of the value upon which the tax was based was vague and discriminatory and that the act was discriminatory in exempting transfers between spouses and between parents and children. The court rejected these arguments and affirmed, holding (1) that the act made clear that both the buyer and seller in a transaction were responsible for payment of the tax, (2) that the definition of value contained in the act was sufficiently certain, and (3) that the act was not discriminatory because of the challenged exemptions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Winger v. Aires


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


371 Pa. 242; 89 A.2d 521; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 415


Argued April 15, 1952  
June 24, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 81 and 82, Jan. T., 1952, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, page 144, Equity Docket, No. 10, in case of Charles B. Winger, Ira B. Winger and Ruth B. Oberholtzer, et al. v. Ray Aires et al. Decree reversed.

Bill in equity to enjoin condemnation proceedings. Before SCHAEFFER, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding for defendants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered dismissing bill. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed, costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their action to enjoin defendant school district from initiating eminent domain proceedings against their farm.


OVERVIEW: The school board met and decided that another school was needed. The school board offered to purchase the owner's farm, but the owners declined. The school board met again and adopted a resolution authorizing the acquisition of the owner's farm by condemnation proceedings. The owners filed an action to enjoin the school district from initiating eminent domain proceedings against their farm. The trial court dismissed their bill of complaint. The owners appealed, and the court reversed. The court found that the question was whether the school board had the authority to take 55 acres of land for a school building that would accommodate 65 pupils. The court held that the evidence demonstrated that the school board's action constituted an abuse of discretion in its exercise of the power of eminent domain. The school board needed only 12 acres. The court articulated that no school board could go into real estate business, even by indirect method of taking by eminent domain more land than was needed and then selling what was remaining. The court noted that what the legislature could not do a school district could not do.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the owner's action to enjoin the school district from initiating eminent domain proceedings against their farm.

Katzin v. McShain


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


371 Pa. 251; 89 A.2d 519; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 416


Argued May 26, 1952  
June 24, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 77, Jan. T., 1952, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1950, No. 4277, in case of Louis Katzin v. John McShain, Chairman et al., constituting the Philadelphia Zoning Board of Adjustment. Order affirmed.

Appeal by property owner from refusal of a registration permit by Zoning Board of Adjustment. Before BLUETT, J.

Judgment entered for defendants. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: We see no error in the proceedings below and the order of Common Pleas Court No. 4, Philadelphia County, is affirmed, with costs to be paid by the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed an order of Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a board's refusal of the owner's request to store trucks on his property, which was zoned "A" commercial.


OVERVIEW: The owner wanted to store trucks on his land. Neighbors objected. The board refused the owner's request for a certificate permitting him to use his property, which was zoned "A" commercial, for storing trucks. The trial court affirmed the board's refusal, stating that the board had not abused its discretion. On appeal, the court affirmed. There was no unconstitutional delegation of police power to the board. The ascertainment of facts must necessarily have been accomplished by a fact-finding body with authority to hear witnesses, analyze the evidence, and render a decision based on criteria established by the statute. The court reviewed the board's decision but did not find that it had acted arbitrarily, capriciously, or in violation of positive law. Had it done so, the court could have called it to account for its defect and the injured party would have been granted another hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Loushay Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


370 Pa. 453; 88 A.2d 793; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 362


Argued April 16, 1952  
May 27, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 115, 116 and 117, Jan. T., 1952, from judgment of Superior Court, Oct. T., 1951, Nos. 85, 86 and 87, affirming judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County, Sept. T., 1950, No. 110, in re Appeals of J. Lloyd Loushay, John E. Snedeker and R. G. C. Jones from Auditor's Report of Bradford County. Judgment affirmed.

Same case in Superior Court: 169 Pa. Super. Ct. 543.

Appeal by county commissioners from surcharge by county auditors. Before ROSENFIELD, P.J.

Order entered directing entry of judgment of surcharge against county commissioners jointly and severally.Commissioners appealed to the Superior Court which affirmed the judgment of the court below. Appeal by commissioners to Supreme Court allowed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the county commissioners, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of the trial court, which directed the entry of the judgment of a surcharge against the commissioners, in the action by the commissioners challenging the report of appellees, the county auditors.


OVERVIEW: The county commissioners, pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 62, § 2253, provided themselves an allowance for expenses. After the provision was revised repealing the allowance, the county auditors issued a report, surcharging them to reimburse the allowance. The commissioners brought an action, challenging the report. The trial court entered judgment for the auditors. On the commissioners' appeal, the intermediate appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court. On further appeal, the court reviewed the record and affirmed the decision of the intermediate appellate court. The court determined that the statute creating an allowance was unconstitutional because it violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 13 which did not allow an increase in the salary or emoluments after election or appointment. Moreover, the allowance had been repealed by implication because of conflicting provisions in a later amendment, pursuant to the Statutory Construction Act, 1937 P. L. 1019, art. V, § 75. Finally, because of public policy, the public funds paid by public officials to themselves, where the authorizing statute had been declared unconstitutional or void, could be recovered by the government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the lower courts.

Bradford Tp. Taxpayers Protective Ass'n v. McKean County Board of Assessment & Revision of Taxes


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


370 Pa. 468; 88 A.2d 782; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 364


Argued April 18, 1952  
May 26, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 88, Jan. T., 1952, from order of Court of Common Pleas of McKean County, Feb. T., 1951, in Equity, No. 3, in case of Bradford Township Taxpayers Protective Association, by Arthur S. Storm, v. McKean County Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes, also known as Commissioners of McKean County. Order affirmed.

Bill in equity.

Defendant's preliminary objections sustained and order entered dismissing bill, opinion by HUBBARD, P.J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: For the above reasons the order must be affirmed.

Order affirmed. Costs to be paid by the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an unincorporated association of taxpayers in a township, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of McKean County (Pennsylvania), in Equity, No. 3, which sustained preliminary objections by defendant, the McKean County Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes, and dismissed a bill. The association contended that a method of assessment was unconstitutional and disregarded the statutes that granted the power to assess.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that equity was without jurisdiction. The court noted that this was not a case of a denial by a property owner of the "power to levy any tax." The association's prayer asked for a reduction of assessments of real estate, other than oil lands, to the same ratio of assessed value to actual or market value as applied to oil lands. The court found that this was a claim that an over assessment of the lands of the association's members had been made. Thus, the court affirmed and concluded that their remedy was by appeal from the assessment. This was a situation where the members complained about an over assessment of their property in comparison with other property in the township, namely, oil lands. If, upon appeal by the members, the trial court found a lack of uniformity or a violation of the statutes, they would have been entitled to appropriate remedial action. However, the remedy was not by a bill in equity. The court's decision was not an adjudication of the validity of the assessment or an approval of the adopted method. The court only decided that every question presented could have been raised on appeal from the revised assessment under the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order with costs to be paid by the association.

Beal v. Reading Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


370 Pa. 45; 87 A.2d 214; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 310


Argued January 9, 1952  
April 1, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 221 and 225, Jan. T., 1951, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1944, No. 1065, in case of Angelina Beal v. Reading Company. Order reversed and judgment entered for defendant.

Trespass for personal injuries. Before BROWN, P.J.

Verdicts, for plaintiff wife in the sum of $5,000., and in favor of plaintiff husband in the sum of $1,000.; defendant's motion for judgment n.o.v. refused but motion for new trial granted. Plaintiff wife, and defendant, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order for new trial and order dismissing defendant's motion for judgment are reversed and judgment is here entered for defendant non obstante veredicto .


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, and defendant railroad company appealed a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted the company's motion for a new trial, and denied its motion for judgment non obstante veredicto in this trespass action.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife brought an action against the company to recover damages for injuries the wife suffered when she stepped into a hole made by the company during the construction of its railroad along the state highway. The trial court entered judgment for the husband and wife. It granted the company's motion for a new trial and dismissed its motion for judgment non obstante veredicto. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment for the husband and wife. It reversed the motion for a new trial and dismissal of the motion for judgment. The court held that the company had no duty to provide lateral support to the highway because the terms of the condemnation proceeding provided that the state only acquire the right to have the company refrain from interfering with the lateral support for the highway. The court ruled that the husband and wife failed to establish causation. Therefore, their claim that the company caused the hole in the highway and was responsible for maintaining a dangerous condition close to the highway was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the company's motion for a new trial and the dismissal of its motion for judgment non obstante veredicto, and affirmed the judgment for the husband and wife.

Schaad v. Hotel Easton Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


369 Pa. 486; 87 A.2d 227; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 289


Argued January 8, 1952  
March 24, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 43, Jan. T., 1952, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Nov. T., 1949, No. 7, in case of Carl E. Schaad and John H. West v. Hotel Easton Company. Decree affirmed.

Bill in equity. Before BARTHOLD, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiffs; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered for plaintiffs. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; the parties to bear their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, preferred stockholders, sought an injunction against defendant corporation to restrain it from proceeding with a reorganization plan wherein the corporate by-laws were to be amended and the outstanding shares of preferred stock, together with the accrued dividends, would be converted into common stock. The Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania) found in favor of the stockholders, and the corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether is whether a dissenting preferred stockholder could be compelled, under a recapitalization scheme, to accept common stock in exchange for his or her holdings, with loss of his or her right to the then accrued, cumulative, undeclared, and unpaid dividends. The corporation asserted that the plan was legal on three grounds: (1) by virtue of the power to amend the by-laws; (2) by virtue of the Act of May 21, 1923, Pa. Laws 288; and (3) by virtue of the Business Corporation Law of May 5, 1933, Pa. Laws 364. The court concluded that the corporation did not have the authority to compel the stockholders to exchange their preferred stock. Merely because a statute may authorize a corporation to refashion its capital structure or reclassify its stock by altering preferential provisions or other terms did not, in the absence of a clear expression of intention to the contrary, warrant an interpretation that would permit the deprivation of dissenting preferred shareholders of their rights in regard to accrued, unpaid, and cumulative dividends.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree of the trial court that enjoined the corporation from proceeding with a reorganization plan. The court ordered that the parties were to bear their respective costs.

The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


369 Pa. 560; 87 A.2d 255; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 297


Argued January 16, 1952  
March 24, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 19, May T., 1952, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, 1947, Commonwealth Docket, No. 252, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Fireman's Fund Insurance Company. Judgment affirmed.

Proceedings upon appeal from decision of Board of Finance and Revenue Refusing petition of defendant for review of tax reassessment.Before RUPP, P.J., RICHARDS, P.J. and WOODSIDE, J., without a jury.

Judgment entered for Commonwealth and against defendant, opinion by RUPP, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign insurance company's claim arose from appellee state's retaliatory charges against appellant, and appellant questioned the constitutionality and application of § 212 of the Act of 1921 in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which ruled in favor of appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant California corporation did fire insurance business in Pennsylvania. A gross premiums tax charge of.5 percent was levied against appellant as a retaliatory charge, and it sued. The court held that § 212 was a comprehensive exposition of the law governing insurance companies, both domestic and foreign, and that the classifications were reasonable as exercises of police power in licensing such companies. The retaliatory charges were valid, and appellee in no way controlled the amount, collection or use of the fire patrol funds which were used to benefit appellant by ending fires. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court construed the statutory application and the constitutionality of the statute to affirm the judgment.

Dunlap Appeal


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


370 Pa. 31; 87 A.2d 299; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 308


Argued January 8, 1952  
March 24, 1952

Appeal by purchaser and by seller of real estate from decision of Zoning Board of Adjustment refusing application for variance.

DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at appellants' cost.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a purchaser and seller, challenged the decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their appeal and exceptions to adjudication and affirmed the decision of a zoning board, which refused appellants' application for a zoning variance.


OVERVIEW: Appellants applied to the zoning board for a zoning variance, which would have permitted appellants to construct row houses in the borough. The board refused the variance and appellants sought review. The lower court dismissed their appeal and affirmed the board's decision. Appellants again sought review, attacking the constitutionality of the ordinance that prohibited row houses on the theory that it violated their vested rights and was an unreasonable classification. Appellants argued that their vested rights stemmed from expenditures for the installation of water, sewer, and gas mains, and street curbing in accordance with an established plan for development of their property. In addition, the ordinance was not directed against appellants and no element of equitable estoppel was presented.

Sarne v. Baltimore & O. R. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


370 Pa. 82; 87 A.2d 264; 1952 Pa. LEXIS 314


Argued November 20, 1951  
March 24, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 193 to 200 and Nos. 204 to 207, inclusive, from order and judgments of Courts of Common Pleas Nos. 6 and 7 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1949, Nos. 255 and 256, in case of Frank Sarne and Walter C. Maddox v. The Baltimore & Ohio Railroad Company et al., Order reversed.

Actions of trespass for personal injuries. Before FENERTY, J.

Verdicts, for plaintiff Maddox and against defendants, construction company and concrete company, in the sum of $2500; and in favor of plaintiff Sarne against same defendants in the sum of $25,000.; verdicts in favor of other defendants; defendants' motions for judgment n.o.v. and new trial refused; new trial awarded by court of its own motion as to all parties, opinion by SMITH, P.J. Plaintiffs and defendants, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of new trial as to defendants Baltimore and Ohio Railroad Company, Lee A. Hauser, an individual trading as Hauser Construction Company, L. E. Winter Co., Inc. and Raymond Concrete Pile Company is reversed; judgment is here granted in favor of Lee A. Hauser, and the record remanded with direction to the court below to enter judgment on the verdicts in favor of the Baltimore and Ohio Railroad [***2] Company and L.E. Winter Co., Inc., and in favor of plaintiff Frank Sarne for $25,000 and in favor of Walter C. Maddox for $2,500 against Raymond Concrete Pile Company.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two workers, in separate trespass actions sought to recover for injuries suffered when an overhead steam pipe fell on them. Verdicts were granted against defendants, general contractor, and concrete company, but no judgment was granted against defendants, railroad company, company, and partnership. The parties challenged the Courts of Common Pleas Nos. 6 and 7, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) grant of a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The railroad company was renovating a roundhouse and had contracted with the general contractor, who employed as subcontractors the partnership, concrete company, and company. The court reversed the grant of a new trial, finding that the evidence was insufficient to hold the railroad company responsible for the injuries because the use of the roadhouse until the steam pipe radiators were disconnected did not establish liability and a new trial should not have been granted. The court sustained the general contractor's appeal because his liability was predicated on the supposition that he had control over the premises. If the general contractor was in control, then the injured workers sole remedy would have been under the workmen's compensation law. The court found that the verdicts against the concrete company should stand because the testimony that its employees permitted the heavy hammer on the pipe driver to hit the pipe and that their other employees pulled the pipe to one side was sufficient to allow the jury to decide that the concrete company was negligent. The grant of a new trial as to the company was reversed because the jury had already passed upon its negligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of a new trial as to the railroad company, general contractor, concrete company, and company. The court granted judgment in favor of the general contractor, and remanded the record with direction to the lower court to enter judgment on the verdicts in favor of the railroad company, and the company. Judgment was entered in favor of the injured workers against the concrete company.
