Northwestern Pennsylvania Automatic Phonograph Ass'n v. Meadville


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


359 Pa. 549; 59 A.2d 907; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 440; 2 A.L.R.2d 913


Submitted May 24, 1948  
July 6, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 109, Jan. T., 1948, from decree of Common Pleas, Crawford Co., Feb. T., 1946 No. 3, in case of Northwestern Pennsylvania Automatic Phonograph Association v. City of Meadville. Decree affirmed.

Bill in equity to enjoin enforcement of ordinance. Before KENT, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding for defendant and decree entered dismissing bill. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Crawford County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the corporation's bill in equity to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance of appellee City.


OVERVIEW: The corporation averred that the City was without power to enact the ordinance. The ordinance levied a license tax upon possessors of pin ball and juke box machines and provided penalties for violation thereof. The trial court dismissed the corporation's exceptions to the action of the chancellor, which entered a decree nisi that dismissed the bill and dissolved a preliminary injunction. The court determined that the pleadings did not reveal, nor did the record establish, that the corporation was in any way subject to the terms of the ordinance. The court explained that the corporation was not subject to any penalty because neither it nor its members possessed pin ball machines or juke boxes within the meaning of the ordinance. The court noted that a party challenging the validity of the legislation had to aver and prove that it was subject to the challenged enactment. The court concluded that dismissal of the bill was proper because the corporation had no standing to maintain the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree of the trial court.

 

510 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Dunkard Twp. Sch. Tax Case


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


359 Pa. 605; 60 A.2d 39; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 450


Argued May 27, 1948  
July 6, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 103, March T., 1948, from order of Quarter Sessions, Greene Co., Dec. Sessions, 1947, No. 71, in Appeal of Certain Taxpayers of Dunkard Township, Greene County. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition and rule by Township taxpayers to set aside ordinance as unconstitutional.

Rule discharged, opinion by HOOK, P.J., Taxpayers appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is affirmed and the appeal dismissed at cost of appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Court of Quarter Sessions of Greene County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their petition to set aside appellee school district's taxing resolution and to enjoin the district from collecting tax under the resolution.


OVERVIEW: After the school district adopted its annual budget and levied taxes, it learned that it was required to give its employees a raise pursuant to the Act of July 5, 1947, P.L. 1266. In order to raise the additional revenue needed, it passed a resolution that taxed the privilege of strip mining coal within the district's county. The taxpayers, contending that the resolution was unconstitutional, filed a petition to set aside the resolution and to enjoin the district from collecting the tax under the resolution. The trial court dismissed the suit, which the court affirmed on appeal. The court held that the resolution did not violate § 502 of the School Code, the Act of May 18, 1911, P.L. 309, because the Act of July 5, 1947, P.L. 1266 expressly gave school districts permission to assess an additional levy in order to satisfy the mandates of Act of July 5, 1947, P.L. 1266. The court found that taxing the privilege of strip mining did not constitute double taxation, and even if it did, double taxation was permissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

511 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Commonwealth


THE SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


359 Pa. 363; 59 A.2d 154; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 408


Argued March 23, 1948  
May 26, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 73 and 74, March T., 1948, from orders of Common Pleas, Allegheny Co., April T., 1947, Nos. 1551 and 1552, respectively, in Matter of Certain Moneys in Possession and Custody of The Union Trust Company of Pittsburgh and in re Peoples-Pittsburgh Trust Company. Order reversed.

Proceedings upon petitions by Commonwealth for payment to it of funds without escheat under the Act of April 9, 1929, P.L. 343.

Petitions dismissed, before McNAUGHER, O'TOOLE and WEISS, JJ., opinion by WEISS, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The orders of the court below are reversed, and the record is remanded with direction to enter orders in accordance with the prayers of the petitions; costs to be paid by appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the state's petitions for payment of funds from appellee bank without escheat under the Act of April 9, 1929, 1929 Pa. Laws 343.


OVERVIEW: The state filed petitions against the bank seeking the payment, without escheat, of certain unclaimed moneys held by the bank as depositories pursuant to the Act of 1919 (Act). The lower court concluded that the Act's publication requirement was optional, and thereby violative of the due process clause of the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions. The lower court dismissed the petitions, and the state appealed. The court held that the required notification of the depositor by mail was in itself sufficient to fulfill the requirements of due process. The court found that because the transfer of the moneys was simply a change of custody and not a confiscation or an ultimate adjudication involving title, and because the deposits could have been reclaimed at any time, the rights of the owners were not affected. The court held that the Act of 1919 did not, in its application to national banks, involve any such interference with their operations or impairment of their efficiency as instrumentalities of the federal government as to render the Act unconstitutional. The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of the state's petitions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court dismissing the state's petitions for payment of funds from the bank without escheat and remanded the case with direction to enter orders in accordance with the state' petitions.

 

512 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


McSorley v. Fitzgerald


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


359 Pa. 264; 59 A.2d 142; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 388


Argued April 20, 1948  
May 24, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction. No. 115, Miscellaneous Docket, March T., 1948, in case of G. Franklin McSorley v. Rufus H. Fitzgerald et al. Bill dismissed.



DISPOSITION: The bill is dismissed; the parties to bear their respective costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought a bill in equity against defendant city, seeking a determination that a law creating a public parking authority was unconstitutional. The parking association and commonwealth were permitted to intervene in the action.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought a bill in equity against the city, seeking to have a law that created a public parking authority declared invalid. The parking association and commonwealth intervened. The court dismissed the bill. The court found that the law in question granted the city the right to create a public parking authority. The authority's purpose, according to the court, was to solve the problems created by traffic congestion on the city's streets, at least part of which was caused by parked cars. The statute granted the authority the power to acquire land through the power of eminent domain. The authority was also exempt from taxes on that property. The court found that the taxpayer's attack on the statute was based on the argument that the purpose for which the parking authority was created was not a public use. The court disagreed, saying that the statute was intended to promote the larger and more general good of the community by freeing the streets of the impediments and perils that arose from traffic congestion. The statute's justification, moreover, arose directly from the exercise of the police power, which the court called the supreme power of the government.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the taxpayer's bill against the city, which had sought to have a law creating a public parking authority declared invalid.

 

513 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Girard Trust Co. v. Philadelphia


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


359 Pa. 319; 59 A.2d 124; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 399


Argued April 20, 1948  
May 24, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 118, Jan. T., 1948, from judgment of Common Pleas No. 2, Philadelphia Co., June T., 1946, No. 2235, in case of Girard Trust Company, Trustee for General Accident, Fire & Life Assurance Corp., Ltd. v. City and County of Philadelphia. Judgment affirmed.

Assumpsit. Before SMITH, P.J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed finding for plaintiff; exceptions to adjudication dismissed in part and final decree entered. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas No. 2, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment for plaintiff trust company in an action in assumpsit to recover certain personal property taxes erroneously paid by the company, as trustee for a foreign corporation.


OVERVIEW: The foreign corporation entered into a written agreement with the trust company whereby the latter became trustee of certain moneys and securities for the benefit of policyholders of the corporation. The purpose of the agreement was to satisfy insurance laws of the various states and thereby enable the corporation to do business in the country. On review, the court affirmed. The intention of the legislature to require a political subdivision to make refund of taxes erroneously or inadvertently paid was clearly expressed not only in the title of the applicable Act, but also in the several provisions thereof. The legislative intention was clearly expressed and administration thereof presented no difficulty. The trust was not subject to the tax. The city's suggestion that it was proper for the court to reexamine and reverse the prior decision amounted to a request for a reargument of that case. That could not be permitted. The lower court properly entered judgment for the full amount of taxes paid with interest. That the company was reimbursed as required by the trust indentures authorizing the issuance of bonds upon which the tax was imposed, did not reduce the amount of the refund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

514 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Warren Borough v. Willey


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


359 Pa. 144; 58 A.2d 454; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 373


Argued April 12, 1948  
April 22, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 104, Jan. T., 1948, from order of C.P., Warren Co., March T., 1947, No. 10, in case of The Burgess and Town Council of Borough of Warren v. Hartwell Willey. Order reversed.

Petition for declaratory judgment.

Judgment entered in favor of plaintiff; opinion by WADE, P.J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order appealed from is reversed, costs to be paid by the plaintiff in the proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fireman appealed the judgment of the Common Pleas Court of Warren County (Pennsylvania) in favor of plaintiff Borough of Warren in the Borough's declaratory judgment action to determine whether or not Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, ch. 355.1, § 22, of the Civil Service Act applied to the fireman employed by the Borough before the Act was passed.


OVERVIEW: The fireman was already employed by the borough when he was elected to be second fire captain for one year. When the year was up, he was demoted without reference to the Civil Service Act passed during the prior year. The Civil Service Commission found that the fireman was demoted without a proper hearing as provided for by the Act. The Borough's right to a declaratory judgment was asserted on the ground that the Act was unconstitutional if construed to apply to the Borough's existing employment contract with the fireman. The trial court found that the fireman was lawfully demoted. Reversing, the court held that the Borough was an agent of the State. Thus, the Borough's relations with its employees were subject to State regulation, and the legislature had the power to make the regulation effective without regard to and in spite of the local regulations. The Act, therefore, necessarily superseded any existing rule or regulation established by the Borough inconsistent therewith, and the Borough council could not demote the fireman without statutory compliance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

515 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Stadtfeld Estate


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


359 Pa. 147; 58 A.2d 478; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 374


Argued March 25, 1948  
April 22, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 53 and 54, March T., 1948, from decree of O.C., Allegheny Co., 1943, No. 10576, in Estate of Joseph Stadtfeld, deceased. Decree affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition by executors to prorate taxes among widow, her trustee and the residuary estate of decedent. Before BOYLE, J.

Adjudication filed finding for petitioners; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered allowing proration, before TRIMBLE, P.J., BOYLE and COX, JJ., opinion by BOYLE, J., dissenting opinion by TRIMBLE, P.J. Widow and widow's trustee, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sought review of a judgment of a circuit court, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which rendered judgment upon petition by appellee executors to prorate taxes among the widow, her trustee, and the residuary estate of decedent.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that even if the widow's status was that of a creditor of her deceased husband's estate for purposes of the state transfer inheritance tax, her claim under the separation agreements was not one deductible, under the federal estate tax law, from the value of his gross estate. The provision in the decedent's will was expressly limited to property passing to legatees and devisees under the will. There was no merit in the widow's contention that the application of the Proration Act impaired the obligation of the contracts between the decedent and his wife. It was elementary that every contract was made with knowledge of the fact that the rights thereunder could have been taxed by the sovereign power, and whatever obligations were assumed by the decedent in the agreements with his wife remained unimpaired notwithstanding the subsequent imposition of the federal estate tax and its apportionment under the Act of 1937. Nor was there any greater merit in the widow's suggestion that there was a contractual obligation on his part to pay any taxes that might thereafter have been imposed upon the payments to be made to his wife or on the trust fund to be established.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Mikell v. School Dist.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


359 Pa. 113; 58 A.2d 339; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 368; 4 A.L.R.2d 962


Argued March 24, 1948  
April 12, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction, in Equity, No. 146, Jan. T., 1948, in case of Thomas P. Mikell, Trustee under will of William E. Mikell, deceased, v. The School District of Philadelphia et al. Bill dismissed.



DISPOSITION: Bill dismissed at plaintiff's costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff testamentary trustee, who was a resident of defendant School District of Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, and as a trustee, held title to intangible personal property, sought to enjoin enforcement of an Act of Assembly, 24 P.S. § 581.1-581.16 (1947) (Act), which imposed a personal property tax upon the residents of first class school districts for public school purposes.


OVERVIEW: The trustee sought to enjoin enforcement of the Act. He argued that it was unconstitutional because it was a revenue-raising measure which originated in the Senate instead of the House of Representatives and was , therefore, in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 14. The trustee also argued that the law had a consequent discriminatory effect, due to a want of uniformity, violating the "right of property" and the "due process" clauses of the Pennsylvania Constitution and the due process and equal protection clauses of the federal constitution. The court entered an order dismissing the trustee's bill. The court held that the Act was not a revenue-raising measure within the meaning of the term as used in the Pennsylvania Constitution because the funds raised by the tax would not be used for the state government's purposes, but instead would go to the school district in which the tax was collected. The court also held that the state constitution clause concerning the place of the origin of a bill for raising revenue was directory, not mandatory; and the Act did not violate the tax uniformity requirement of Pa. Const. art. IX, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order dismissing plaintiff's bill.

Dufour v. Maize


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


358 Pa. 309; 56 A.2d 675; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 303; 1 A.L.R.2d 563


Argued December 2, 1947  
January 19, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 9, May T., 1948, from decree of C.P., Dauphin Co., 1945, Equity Docket, No. 1721, Commonwealth Docket, No. 93, in case of Alexander Dufour v. Richard Maize, Secretary of Mines et al. Decree affirmed.

Bill in equity attacking constitutionality of Bituminous Coal Open Pit Mining Conservation Act. Before RICHARDS, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding Act constitutional and order entered dismissing bill. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed at the costs of appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant coal mine operator filed a bill in equity against appellees, state Secretary of Mines and others attacking the constitutionality of the Bituminous Coal Open Pit Mining Conservation Act (Act), 52 P.S. § 1396.1. The trial court (Pennsylvania) entered a judgment finding the Act constitutional and an order dismissing the bill. After a rehearing the court again entered a final decree dismissing the bill, from which the operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth passed legislation pertaining to the reclamation of pit or strip mines used to mine bituminous coal. The Act required that an operator pay fees and acquire bonds prior to operating a strip or pit mine. It also required replanting of trees or shrubs after the mine was closed or abandoned. The fees collected by the state were used exclusively for reforesting the closed mines. The coal mine operator filed a bill in equity to enjoin the enforcement of the Act and claimed it was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment against him at the original trial and on his petition for rehearing. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the fees were not special taxes in violation of the state constitution, and that the classification of mining operations was rational. There was no deprivation of due process or the illegal taking of property by the imposition of the fees. The fees were not appropriations and it was permissible for the fees to be used for reclamation and reforestation projects for as long as the underlying Act was in effect. The court held that the licensing fee was not a tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree that held that the act was not unconstitutional and that dismissed the coal mine operator's lawsuit to prevent enforcement of the act.

In re Escheat of Moneys, etc.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


358 Pa. 133; 57 A.2d 256; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 277


Submitted December 4, 1947  
January 5, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 208, Jan. T., 1947, from decree of C.P. No. 4, Dec. T., 1945, No. 3290, in the Matter of Escheat of Moneys deposited in and under the control of the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Pennsylvania. Decree reversed.

Proceeding upon petition by State Escheator for escheat of funds in the Treasury of the United States from the Eastern District Court. Before BLUETT, J., without a jury.

Order of escheat entered for the Commonwealth. United States of America appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is reversed and the petition dismissed. Costs to be paid by appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, an escheator of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, filed a petition for the escheat of funds that were deposited into the United States Treasury. Appellant, the United States, sought review of the decree of a court of common pleas (Pennsylvania), which granted the escheator's petition and which entered an order of escheat for the Commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: Unclaimed wages and effects of deceased seamen were deposited into the United States Treasury pursuant to ch. 389 of the Act of 1897 (Federal Act of 1897), 29 Stat. 689, as amended by 46 U.S.C.S. § 628. The escheator claimed that the Commonwealth had the power to determine the escheat of property under § 5 of the Act of 1889 (Pennsylvania Act of 1889), P.L. 66, as amended by § 2 of the Act of 1935, P.L. 475, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 27, § 41, and that the Commonwealth was entitled to the funds. The United States claimed that the trial court's decree for the escheator violated the Federal Act of 1897. The court reversed the trial court's decree. The court held that the Commonwealth's power to determine the escheat of property within its jurisdiction did not extend to subject-matter over which Congress had exercised its power and that Congress exercised its power by the enactment of the Federal Act of 1897. The court also held that the Federal Act of 1897 negated the Commonwealth's power over the funds and that the Pennsylvania Act of 1889 was inapplicable. The court further held that the Commonwealth was not entitled to the funds and that the escheator's petition should be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decree for the Commonwealth and dismissed the escheator's petition.

358 Pa. 252; 56 A.2d 250; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 295

January 5, 1948

Audit of account of executrices. Before APPEL, P.J.

Adjudication filed allowing claims of Commonwealth and Lancaster County Institution District; exceptions to adjudication dismissed. Legatee appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daughter sought review of a judgment of the Orphans' Court of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed her exceptions to an award of the entire balance of her mother's estate for the purpose of paying for the support and institutional care of another daughter and that daughter's children.


OVERVIEW: One of the deceased mother's children was institutionalized and as a result financial liabilities for her care and for the care of her children cumulated. The orphans' court made the award, and the daughter appealed. The court affirmed. The mother had a financial obligation under the law to support her children and grandchildren. Commonwealth v. Central R. Co.


The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania


358 Pa. 326; 58 A.2d 173; 1948 Pa. LEXIS 304


Argued November 26, 1947  
January 5, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 24, May T., 1946, from decree of C.P., Dauphin Co., 1940, Commonwealth Docket, No. 1648, in case of Commonwealth v. Central Railroad Company of New Jersey. Decree affirmed; reargument refused March 24, 1948.

Proceeding upon petition and rule by defendant to show cause why a judgment confessed by plaintiff in favor of defendant and credited to defendant's account upon a claim for tax refund should not be stricken off.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, sought review of a decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which struck off a judgment entered by the Attorney General against the Commonwealth and entered a judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer, a railroad company.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, pursuant to the Fiscal Code, Act of 1929, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 1104, appealed to the lower court from an order of the Board of Finance and Revenue refusing a resettlement of tax liability. The Attorney General, without the taxpayer's consent, filed what purported to be a confession of judgment. The taxpayer filed its petition to show cause why said judgment should not be stricken off, alleging that the Attorney General had no authority to enter the judgment and the taxpayer did not consent to entry of the judgment. The court held that the completeness with which the legislature had, by art. 522 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stortecky


No. 462, April T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


238 Pa. Super. 117; 352 A.2d 491; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2568


April 18, 1975, Submitted  
December 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County, Dec. T., 1973, No. 7460A, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. John Stortecky.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, which was rendered upon appellants' convictions for the crimes of resisting arrest, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5104, and aggravated assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was placed under arrest when he refused to leave an area at the request of police, and while being arrested, appellant assaulted and battered the person of the arresting officer. Appellant was convicted of and sentenced for resisting arrest, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5104, and aggravated assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2702(a)(3). Appellant contended that the lower court erred in failing in its charge to define "lawful arrest" in the language requested by appellant's counsel, which was a term involved in each of the offenses for which appellant was convicted. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that the trial judge was not required to place the question of lawfulness of appellant's arrest before the jury. Rather, that question, which was whether there was probable cause for the arrest, was within the province of the court, not the jury. The court found that there was ample evidence that supported probable cause of the officers to arrest appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence, which was rendered upon appellant's conviction for resisting arrest and aggravated assault, because the determination of whether there was probable cause for appellant's arrest was within the province of the trial judge, not the jury, so the trial judge was not required to define "lawful arrest" for the jury in the language requested by appellant.

 

523 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Colding


No. 1175, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


237 Pa. Super. 612; 352 A.2d 554; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2496


March 24, 1975, Submitted  
December 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Oct. T., 1972, No. 1938, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Ernest Colding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to a term of confinement that was more than the minimum initial sentence by the court. Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. He contended that the new sentence was in excess of the initial sentence and, therefore, violated his right against double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery and initially sentenced to to four years. Upon reconsideration, he was sentenced instead to probation. When he violated his probation, it was revoked and he was sentenced to a term that was for one and one-half to three years. The court affirmed the judgment of the sentence because it found that, whether a sentence was stated in terms of minimum and maximum, the maximum sentence was the real sentence. The maximum sentence was the only portion with legal validity. Therefore, because the initial sentence was for up to four years, the subsequent revocation of parole and new sentence for one and one-half to three years was less than the maximum sentence. Therefore, it did not violate double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's sentence that followed the revocation of his probation, which followed a reconsideration of an initial sentence. The court found that it was the maximum term of the initial sentence, or four years, that the trial court could not exceed when it issued the new sentence of one and one-half to three years. Therefore, appellant's freedom from double jeopardy was not violated.

 

524 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Krasner


No. 711, Oct. T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


238 Pa. Super. 1; 352 A.2d 479; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2574


June 12, 1975, Argued  
December 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Jan. T., 1972, Nos. 725, 726, and 727, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. John Krasner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed and appellant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult book store owner sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him for unlawful possession of obscene literature with intent to sell, with the exhibition of obscene moving pictures, and with conspiracy. Appellant contended that his motion for a new trial should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant adult book store owner was arrested for unlawful possession of obscene literature with intent to sell, with the exhibition of obscene moving pictures, and with conspiracy. His motions in arrest of judgment and for a new trial were denied. The court reversed the judgment and discharged appellant. The court found that new case law had required that state statutes designed to regulate obscene materials had to be carefully limited and, because it was enacted before the seminal case, 18 P.S. § 4524 did not specifically define the proscribed conduct. Therefore, technically appellant did not have notice of the proscribed conduct and could not be convicted thereof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant adult book store owner's conviction and discharged appellant. The court found that because the Pennsylvania Penal Code specifically define the proscribed conduct, as required by case law handed down subsequent to the enactment of the statute, appellant did not have the requisite notice to uphold his conviction and sentence.

 

525 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Betres


No. 79, April T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


237 Pa. Super. 361; 352 A.2d 495; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2463; 98 A.L.R.3d 687


April 15, 1975, Argued  
December 1, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, June T., 1974, No. 134, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Peter Betres.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of various gambling charges under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5513(a)(2)-(4). Appellant contended that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of soliciting people to visit his club for unlawful gambling and that the jury should have been informed that gambling, in itself, was not against the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of various gambling charges. Police officers had visited the club bought by appellant and witnessed him controlling a gambling game of dice and controlling who had entrance to the club. The court affirmed appellant's convictions for allowing persons to collect and assemble for the purpose of unlawful gambling at any place under his control, under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5513(a)(2), because the officers had witnessed the control and activities. The court also affirmed appellant's conviction for owning and permitting his property for the use of unlawful gambling, under 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 5513(a)(4), because the deed to the property was in appellant's name. However, the court reversed his conviction for solicitation of any person to visit the unlawful gambling place, under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5513(a)(4), because there was insufficient evidence to convict him of it; the men were already in the club when the officers arrived. The case was remanded for the trial court to determine whether the court's determination required a change in appellant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for allowing persons to unlawfully gamble in his club and to permit the same to occur. However, the court reversed the conviction for the alleged solicitation of others for unlawful gambling because there was insufficient evidence. The court also found that appellant's proposed jury instruction was irrelevant because it was shown that he owned the club. The case was remanded for resentencing.

 

526 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Marshall v. Gedney


No. 1286, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


237 Pa. Super. 372; 352 A.2d 528; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2465


December 2, 1974, Submitted  
December 1, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Nov. T., 1973, No. 0013, and Sept. T., 1973, No. 0357, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Ruby Marshall v. Dewaine Gedney, Director, Release on Recognizance Program.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant relator sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee commonwealth's request to extradite appellant to Kansas under the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, 19 P.S. § 191.15.


OVERVIEW: Kansas, the demanding state presented extradition papers pursuant to 19 P.S. § 191.15, to appellee commonwealth to have appellant relator extradited. Appellee claimed that there was not sufficient probable cause for the arrest. The trial court granted the extradition, and appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied. Appellant sought review of the denial of the writ of habeas corpus in the supreme court, which granted a supersedeas and transferred the matter to the court. The court affirmed the extradition because the papers complied with 19 P.S. § 191.3. The requirements for an extradition were that appellant was charged with a crime in Kansas, that appellant was a fugitive from Kansas, that the subject of the extradition was present in Kansas when the crime was committed, and that he requisition papers were in order, which were accepted as prima facie true. The court found that a requirement to prove probable cause for the arrest could not have been added to the statute. The court also found that if there was no probable cause for the arrest, appellant could have made that challenge in Kansas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for appellee commonwealth to extradite appellant relator to Kansas and held that the extradition papers satisfied the statutory requirements, which did not require sufficient probable cause to arrest appellant and that appellee was unable to add a requirement.

Weber v. Lynch


Nos. 156 and 159, April T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


237 Pa. Super. 48; 346 A.2d 363; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1747


April 18, 1975, Argued  
October 28, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from order of Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Allegheny County, July T., 1972, No. 2156, in case of Ruth M. Weber and C. Kenneth Weber, her husband v. Mary Katherine Lynch v. Newton M. Weir.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, arbitration defendants, challenged the decision of the en banc Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted a new trial to appellees, arbitration plaintiffs, in their challenge to an arbitration award, after the trial judge precluded them from offering testimony from a witness who did not testify at the arbitration hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, arbitration plaintiffs, obtained an arbitration award against appellants, arbitration defendants, but challenged the award as unsatisfactory. Pursuant to a local court rule, the trial court precluded appellees from offering testimony of a physician who had not testified at the arbitration hearing. The lower considered appellees' post-trial motions en banc, and reversed the decision of the trial judge and granted a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the local court rule, which limited the use in arbitration award appeals of witnesses who had not been used at arbitration hearing, contravened the express mandate of the Arbitration Act, 5 P.S. § 21 et seq., that all appeals should be de novo, and exceeded the rule-making authority of the common pleas court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a new trial to appellees, arbitration plaintiffs, because the local court rule that limited the use of witnesses on appeals from arbitration awards contravened a mandate that such appeals were de novo and impermissibly exceeded the rule making authority of the common pleas courts.

 

528 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eshelman


No. 1196, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


236 Pa. Super. 223; 345 A.2d 286; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1702


March 20, 1975, Submitted  
September 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Blair County, No. 137 of 1974, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Larry Chester Eshelman.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his judgment of sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County (Pennsylvania) for possession of marijuana and possession with intent to deliver marijuana.


OVERVIEW: An auxiliary policeman was walking through private property when he saw a package in an abandoned car. He opened the package and found marijuana. Appellant confessed that the marijuana was his. After he was convicted of drug possession, appellant argued that the original warrantless search was illegal. The reviewing court disagreed. A search by a private individual is not subject to the restraints of U.S. Const. amend. IV. Where the search is conducted solely by a private citizen without police knowledge, and the results are later turned over to a proper law enforcement agency for further action, the evidence is admissible. Here, the evidence was admissible because the auxiliary policeman was a private citizen. Under, 53 P.S. § 735, the authority of auxiliary police officers is in effect only while they are on active duty. Here, the officer was not on active duty.


OUTCOME: Appellant's judgment of sentence for possession of marijuana and possession with intent to deliver marijuana was affirmed because an auxiliary policeman was not on active duty when he searched appellant's property without a warrant, so the search was legal.

 

529 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Policino v. Ehrlich


No. 506, Oct. T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


236 Pa. Super. 19; 345 A.2d 224; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1662


June 12, 1975, Argued  
September 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, No. 70-08771, in case of Linda Policino, a minor, by Albert A. Hartman and Lillian R. Hartman, her parents and natural guardians, and Albert A. Hartman and Lillian R. Hartman v. Alan Jeffery Ehrlich and Leonard Policino, additional defendant.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee husband's motion to strike judgment as violative of the statute on interspousal immunity, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 48, § 111. Appellant contended that because appellee failed to plead immunity, object, or appeal the judgment, any error was waived, and that the motion was an impermissible collateral attack on the judgment.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted appellee husband's motion to strike judgment, appellant wife challenged the decision. The court affirmed. First, the motion to strike judgment was proper because under the doctrine of marital immunity, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 48, § 111, appellant could not recover from appellee. Moreover, a motion to strike judgment was appellee's only remedy because although the interspousal immunity doctrine precluded appellant from suing appellee, it did not prevent the original defendant from joining appellee as an additional defendant. Therefore, because the judgment rendered for appellant was defective on its face, it was properly stricken. Further, the motion to strike was not an impermissible collateral attack on the judgment. The motion was a direct attack because appellee sought to remove the judgment, rather than merely negate its effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order striking judgment because pursuant to the interspousal immunity doctrine, appellant wife could not recover from appellee husband and thus the judgment was defective on its face. Further, because appellee's motion sought to remove the judgment, rather than merely negate its effect, it was not an impermissible collateral attack.

531 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Mace


No. 114, March T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 463; 341 A.2d 505; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1548


March 10, 1975, Argued  
June 24, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 1136 C.D. of 1973, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Wayne McArthur Mace.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of sentence from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), entered upon a jury verdict, which found him guilty of involuntary manslaughter in connection with a death caused by a bungled abortion attempt, committed before such operations were legally available.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter in connection with the death of a woman from a bungled abortion attempt. On review, appellant alleged that he was denied due process because he was unable to examine independently certain autopsy specimens. The court found that the commonwealth cooperated fully with the defense, agreeing to permit inspection of all the hospital records, the slides made from body tissue, in fact everything the commonwealth's witnesses had except body fluids and the actual parts of the victims body. Furthermore, the doctor who had chemically analyzed the blood and tissue taken from the body was made available to confer with the defense and its expert prior to trial. Under these circumstances, the court concluded that the commonwealth had not overborne appellant by secretly amassing evidence or designing a case unfairly weighted against him. Accordingly, the judgment of sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed because appellant was not denied due process where he was unable to examine independently certain autopsy specimens. Further, the lower court did not err in refusing to dismiss the charge of involuntary manslaughter when the commonwealth failed to prove its original theory of misdemeanor manslaughter.

Leach v. Philadelphia Sav. Fund Soc.


No. 1380, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 486; 340 A.2d 491; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1550


March 18, 1975, Argued  
June 24, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Feb. T., 1969, No. 655, in case of Omega Leach v. Philadelphia Savings Fund Society, [the correct corporate name being Philadelphia Saving Fund Society] Haverstick-Borthwick Co., McIntire, Magee & Brown and Bausch & Lomb, Inc., and A.L.K. Corp., and Leonard Shaffer Associates, Additional Defendants.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker was injured when a ceiling installed 26 years earlier fell on him. He filed suit against the owners of the property for the 26-year period, including appellee saving fund society, in the Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania). Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment based on 12 P.S. § 65.1. The motion was granted and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant worker was injured when a ceiling installed 26 years earlier fell on him. Appellant brought suit against the installer of the ceiling and three record owners of the property, including appellee saving fund society, who owned the building at the time the ceiling was installed. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment based on 12 P.S. § 65.1 (Supp. 1974-75), which provided a 12-year limitations period for actions brought against persons who performed or furnished the design, planning, supervision or observation of construction, or construction of improvements to real property. The trial court granted appellee's motion, and appellant sought review. The court stated held the summary judgment was premature and inappropriate.

The statute was intended to protect persons lawfully performing or furnishing the design, planning, supervision or observation of construction, or construction of real property improvements.

 

533 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Henderson


No. 1681, Oct. T., 1973


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 525; 341 A.2d 195; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1557


June 10, 1974, Argued  
June 24, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Feb. T., 1973, No. 445, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Shirley Henderson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of sentence from the Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), contending that the lower court erred in considering the maximum sentence for the crime of involuntary manslaughter because the crime occurred prior to the effective date of the new criminal code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant guilty of the charge of involuntary manslaughter and imposed a sentence. Appellant challenged the judgment of sentence on the grounds that the trial court relied upon the new criminal code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 2504 and 1104(1), that became effective after the date of the crime. The court vacated the judgment of sentence and remanded for reconsideration of the sentence. Appellant's offense was governed by the prior law, rather than the new code. Although the sentence was lawful under the prior law, it was apparent that the trial court intended to impose less than the maximum term under the new code. Thus, it was possible that the trial court was influenced by the increased severity under the new code and that the trial court might have imposed a lesser sentence if it had considered the lesser lawful sentence under the prior law.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's judgment of sentence and remanded for reconsideration of the sentence. Appellant was prejudiced by the trial court's consideration of an erroneous maximum sentence under a new criminal code because a lesser sentence might have been imposed if the trial court considered the lesser maximum sentence that was provided for in the statute in effect when the offense was committed.

Commonwealth v. McKennion


No. 104, March T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


235 Pa. Super. 160; 340 A.2d 889; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1599


March 10, 1975, Submitted  
June 24, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Nos. 2364 and 2365 of 1973, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Lawrence P. McKennion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which convicted and sentenced him of theft by unlawful taking or disposition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant admitted to stealing several typewriters and a calculator. The trial court convicted him of theft by unlawful taking or disposition. Appellant challenged the conviction, claiming that the statute under which he was convicted, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3901 (1972), was unconstitutional because it included the element of value as an element of the offense. Appellant also claimed that the requirement that that the value of the property be proven at sentencing violated his presumption of innocence. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, finding that there was no element of value required under the theft statute, but rather value was relevant only to establish the grade of the offense for purpose of sentencing. The court further held that introduction of evidence of value at sentencing did not run afoul of appellant's presumption of innocence, because at the time of sentencing, he had already been adjudicated guilty of the offense.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed because the statute under which he was convicted was not unconstitutional, and the proof of value required at sentencing did not unconstitutionally force him to incriminate himself, or violate his presumption of innocence.

Commonwealth v. Miller


Nos. 34 and 36, March T., 1975


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 146; 339 A.2d 573; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1514


March 10, 1975, Submitted  
April 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County, Nos. 449 and 479 of 1973, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Eddie Leonard Miller and Same v. Rickey Alonso Kauffman.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County (Pennsylvania) that convicted them of criminal conspiracy in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903 (1973) and criminal mischief in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3304 (1973).


OVERVIEW: A fire tower was completely destroyed. The tower fell on a power line, broke a transformer, and put a community out of electrical service. A witness testified for the prosecution that appellants sawed down the fire tower. The witness told police where to go to find the saw used in the crime. Charges were brought against appellants. The trial judge found appellants guilty of criminal conspiracy in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903 (1973) and criminal mischief in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3304 (1973). Appellants sought review. The court found that criminal mischief was a felony of the third degree if appellants intentionally caused pecuniary loss in excess of $ 5,000, or a substantial impairment of a public service. The valuation portion of the statute did not apply to appellants because there was evidence they caused an impairment of a public service, and their conviction for third degree criminal mischief was affirmed. Appellants' convictions for both criminal conspiracy and criminal mischief were proper because the crime of conspiracy did not merge with the completed offense but remained a separate and distinct crime.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court that convicted appellants of both criminal conspiracy and criminal mischief was affirmed because the crime of conspiracy did not merge with the completed offense but remained a separate and distinct crime. Appellants' conviction for third degree criminal mischief was supported by the evidence because they cause the substantial impairment of a public service.

Commonwealth ex rel. Finken v. Roop


No. 199, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 155; 339 A.2d 764; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1515


March 26, 1974, Argued  
April 22, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Reargument Refused May 23, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Oct. T., 1973, No. 71, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Charles Finken, Jr., v. John W. Roop, Administrator of Allentown State Hospital.



DISPOSITION: Order of commitment reversed and appellant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which civilly committed him under 50 P.S. § 4406 of the Pennsylvania Mental Health and Retardation Act of 1966. Appellant claimed that § 4406 failed to provide an individual the procedural and substantive due process required by U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to charges of sodomy and corrupting the morals of a minor. Appellant was committed to a state hospital pursuant to 50 P.S. § 4410 of the Pennsylvania Mental Health and Retardation Act of 1966. Appellant was released after a psychiatrist found that appellant no longer required confinement in a mental institution. A subsequent commitment proceeding under 50 P.S. § 4408 was foreclosed because appellant was not guilty of any technical probation violation. Upon a motion initiated by the state, appellant was subsequently civilly committed under 50 P.S. § 4406. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of § 4406 on appeal. The order of commitment was reversed by the court on appeal and appellant was discharged after the court found § 4406 to have been unconstitutionally vague. Specifically, the court found that § 4406's requirement that the subject's mental illness render him in "need of care" was so broad as to be virtually meaningless. The court explained that the statute needed to make it clear that persons were not to be committed unless there was a substantial likelihood that the person would commit acts which threaten himself or society.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which civilly committed appellant under the Pennsylvania Mental Health and Retardation Act of 1966, was reversed and appellant was discharged after the court found the state's civil commitment statute to have been unconstitutionally vague.

 

537 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stawinsky


No. 245, April T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


234 Pa. Super. 308; 339 A.2d 91; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1532


November 14, 1974, Argued  
April 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County, Nov. T., 1973, No. 7306889A, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Joseph F. Stawinsky.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and case remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that sustained defendant's demurrer to the evidence to the charge of selling drugs in violation of the Pennsylvania Controlled Substance, Drug, Device, and Cosmetic Act, 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113. Commonwealth maintained that it did not have to prove that defendant was not registered under the Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with delivery of a controlled substance in violation of Section 13 of the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act, 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113. He demurred to the evidence on the ground that commonwealth had failed to prove that he was not registered with the Secretary of Health. The trial court sustained that demurrer. On appeal, commonwealth contended that it was not required to establish defendant was not registered in order to establish his violation of the Act. Section 6 of the Act permitted registered persons to manufacture, distribute, retail, sell, offer for sale, and solicit the purchase of controlled substances, and made those persons exempt from the prohibitions of the Act. The court reviewed Section 6 of the Act and the distinction between an exemption and an excuse as delineated under Pennsylvania law. The court then concluded that commonwealth did not have to prove that defendant was not registered in order to establish a violation of the Act. Rather, case law dictated that defendant had to prove the registration issue. The court thus reversed the trial court's order, and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that sustained defendant's demurrer to the evidence was reversed. Defendant, rather than commonwealth, bore the burden of establishing that he was registered with the Pennsylvania Secretary of Health, and therefore permitted to manufacture, distribute, retail, sell, offer for sale, and solicit the purchase of controlled substances under Pennsylvania law.

Commonwealth v. Burak


No. 391, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


232 Pa. Super. 499; 335 A.2d 820; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1409


September 12, 1974, Argued  
March 31, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, March T., 1969, No. 1958, and Aug. T., 1969, Nos. 760, 761 and 762, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Marvin Burak.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence on charges of obscene exhibition and conspiracy to commit an obscene exhibition reversed and defendant discharged; judgment of sentence on charge of corrupting the morals of a minor child affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) convicting him of obscene exhibition, disorderly house, conspiracy to conduct an obscene exhibition and corrupting the morals of a minor child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was manager at a club. The club contained models that were photographed in the nude during sessions. One of the models was a minor under the age of 18. Appellant was convicted of obscene exhibition, disorderly house, conspiracy to conduct an obscene exhibition, and corrupting the morals of a minor child. On review, appellant claimed that the modeling session was not an exhibition and therefore not subject to 18 P.S. § 4528, which related to obscene exhibitions. The court ruled that there was ample evidence for a jury to conclude that the activities by the "models" were indeed an exhibition conducted for profit by appellant. However, the court held that a section in the statute did not specify or defined the conduct that it prohibited. It also held that the evidence was sufficient to convict appellant of corrupting the morals of a minor child. Appellant, as manager of the club, exerted a certain amount of control over the activities therein. Therefore, the judgment on the charges of obscene exhibition and conspiracy to commit an obscene exhibition was reversed and the judgment on the charge of corrupting the morals of a minor child was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the charges of obscene exhibition and conspiracy to commit an obscene exhibition against appellant, but affirmed the judgment on the charge of corrupting the morals of a minor child. The evidence was sufficient to convict appellant of corrupting the morals of a minor child, but the statute did not specify or define the conduct that it prohibited.

 

540 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rooney


No. 1305, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


233 Pa. Super. 225; 335 A.2d 710; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1451


December 3, 1974, Argued  
March 31, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Nos. 422 and 423 of 1970, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Thomas Rooney.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which revoked appellant's probation for three separate charges of fraudulent conversion due to his failure to pay restitution as ordered, and imposed concurrent sentences on the three bills of indictment of not less than one month nor more then five years plus restitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to three separate charges of fraudulent conversion, to which the trial judge imposed costs of prosecution, payment to the county in lieu of a fine, restitution, and probation. Appellant failed to pay restitution. The trial court revoked probation and imposed concurrent sentences on the three bills of indictment of not less than one month nor more than five years plus restitution. On appeal, the court rejected appellant's argument that the trial court could not place appellant on probation as it also had imposed a fine, because the court found that the original sentences required appellant to pay the county in lieu of a fine. There was no violation of double jeopardy because no specific prison sentence term had been originally pronounced. Thus, the trial judge was thus free to impose any sentence after the probation violation not in excess of the maximum fixed by law. Nor did the trial court err in finding appellant willfully violated a condition of his probation, as appellant's excuse of indigency for not paying restitution turned on his credibility, which was within the province of the trial judge to decide. Therefore, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Revocation of appellant's probation for his failure to pay restitution in relation to his convictions for fraudulent conversion was affirmed, as the trial court was free to impose any sentence after the probation violation that was not in excess of the maximum sentence fixed by law, and there was no error in the trial court's finding of appellant's willful violation of his probation.

 

541 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Houck


No. 794, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


233 Pa. Super. 512; 335 A.2d 389; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1483


December 2, 1974, Submitted  
March 31, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, No. 881 of 1973, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Kenneth Houck.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed as to dismissal of the indictment; order placing one half the costs on prosecutor, Leinbach, vacated and the same placed on the County of Berks.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed a criminal complaint against appellee that alleged a violation of the Pennsylvania Crimes Code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5504, by harassment by communication or address, and dividing the costs between appellee and the party who initiated the complaint, who was found to be the "real prosecutor."


OVERVIEW: Complainant had been bothered by telephone calls that he claimed came from appellee. A criminal complaint was signed against appellee alleging a violation of the Pennsylvania Crimes Code (Crimes Code), 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5504. The trial court entered an order dismissing the case under the Crimes Code, § 312, and divided the costs between appellee and complainant, whom the trial judge found was the "real prosecutor." Appellant commonwealth sought review, arguing that the trial court abused his discretion in dismissing the case and that the trial court erred in placing one half the costs on complainant. The trial court had pointed out that complainant and appellee had known each other for years, and that appellant's proof was deficient in showing an intent to harass by the calls. As § 312 allowed for dismissal of "de minimus infractions," the court concluded that the trial court had refused to let the parties' trifling matter proceed to verdict by properly invoking § 312. However, because there was no statutory authority for the assessment of costs against complainant or appellee, the order placing one half the costs on complainant was vacated and the same was placed on the county.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of criminal complaint against defendant for harassment by communication or address was affirmed because the trial court properly invoked a statute that allowed for the dismissal of de minimus infractions. However, that portion of the trial court's order placing one half the costs on complainant as being the "real prosecutor" was vacated because there was no statutory authority for doing so; such costs were thus placed on the county.

 

542 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Doria


No. 1250, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


232 Pa. Super. 439; 335 A.2d 472; 1975 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1398


September 13, 1974, Argued  
February 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Feb. T., 1959, Nos. 786 and 787, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Anthony Doria.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), denying defendant's Post Conviction Hearing Act, 19 P.S. §§ 1180-1, petition, seeking eligibility for conviction relief, alleging that the conviction was based on perjured evidence, among other things. Defendant was convicted of cheating by fraudulent pretenses and fraudulent conversion, and his sentence was a fine on each bill.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of cheating by fraudulent pretenses and fraudulent conversion, and was sentenced to a fine on each bill. The conviction was affirmed by the superior court in 1960. In 1974, defendant filed a Post Conviction Hearing Act (PCHA), 19 P.S. §§ 1180-1, petition. The petition alleged the conviction was based on perjured evidence and constitutional denials, among other things. The trial court dismissed the petition without a hearing, relying on case law that defendant's claims were moot. The superior court affirmed the order. The PCHA provided in part that defendant had to prove that he was incarcerated, at the time of filing the petition, under a sentence of death or imprisonment, or on parole or probation. Defendant complied with his sentence about 14 years ago; therefore, the sentence did not affect directly any subsequent criminal prosecution or conviction to fit into the collateral criminal consequences rule to expand relief eligibility under the PCHA. Eligibility should not be extended to speculative subsequent criminal or civil consequences and should be limited to direct criminal consequences.


OUTCOME: The superior court affirmed an order dismissing defendant's petition under the Post Conviction Hearing Act (PCHA) as moot because a satisfied sentence from 14 years earlier, for a cheating by fraudulent pretenses and fraudulent conversion conviction, did not affect any subsequent criminal prosecution to fit into the collateral criminal consequences rule to expand relief eligibility under the PCHA.

Commonwealth v. Kuykendall


No. 668, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


231 Pa. Super. 457; 331 A.2d 686; 1974 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1361


June 10, 1974, Submitted  
December 11, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Adams County, Feb. T., 1974, No. 108, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Earl William Kuykendall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him to one to two years' incarceration after appellant entered a plea of guilty to the crime of receiving stolen goods.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to receiving stolen goods, and was sentenced to one to two years' incarceration. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although appellant argued that it was unconstitutional to require him to prove the value of the items stolen in a burglary, the court noted that appellant was only charged with burglary and theft, but never had the burden of proving the stolen items' value because those charges were dropped in exchange for his guilty plea to receiving stolen property. The court held that it would not be proper to allow appellant to enter into a plea bargain, plead guilty, and then, on appeal, raise an issue for the first time as to the constitutionality of the act defining the offense. The court also held that appellant's sentence was within the statutory limits and was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence on his guilty plea to receiving stolen property, because appellant never had the burden of proving the value of what was stolen where burglary charges against him were dropped in exchange for his plea, and because the sentence was within statutory limits.

Commonwealth v. Nelson


Nos. 1768 and 1788, Oct. T., 1973


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


230 Pa. Super. 89; 326 A.2d 598; 1974 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2418


June 11, 1974, Submitted  
September 23, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from order of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Nov. T., 1972, Nos. 1205, 1207 and 1208, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Caesar Nelson.



DISPOSITION: Action of trial court quashing indictment charging defendant with conspiracy to bribe government officers and employees on June 28, 1971, affirmed, and decision reversed as to indictment charging defendant with bribery on June 25, 1971, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth sought review from an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), in which indictments were quashed upon the request of the defendant for bribery and conspiring to bribe members of the Philadelphia police department after defendant's appeal for a trial de novo after his conviction in Municipal Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted with two co-defendants for bribery and conspiring to bribe members of the vice squad of the Philadelphia police department. On June 25, 1971, the co-defendant met with an officer and arranged for him to meet with defendant. At the meeting, defendant paid the officer $ 150 and offered to continue payments in exchange for protection of his lottery operation. Immediately after this arrangement the second co-defendant agreed to pay the officer $ 120 per month for the same protection. The officer met with the co-defendants on June 28, 1971 where he received the $ 120. The defendant appealed for a trial de novo after he was convicted and was subsequently indicted for bribery on June 25th and conspiracy to commit bribery on June 28. The trial court quashed the indictments. The court affirmed the quash of the June 28th indictment, holding that the Commonwealth could not indict on offenses not charged in the Municipal Court where defendant had no preliminary hearing. The court reversed and remanded the June 25th indictment, holding that the court could allow amendment of an indictment where two separate offenses were charged in a single indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the quashing of the indictment charging defendant with conspiracy to bribe government officers on June 28th because the indictment charged offenses defendant was not convicted for in Municipal Court and no preliminary hearing was had; the court reversed and remanded as to the indictment charging defendant with bribery on June 25th because the court could allow an indictment to be amended where it was defective in form.

 

546 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Weiner


No. 1989, Oct. T., 1973


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


230 Pa. Super. 245; 326 A.2d 896; 1974 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2442


June 10, 1974, Argued  
September 23, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, No. 300 of 1973, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Max Weiner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of disorderly conduct for violation of 18 P.S. § 4406, on the grounds that his conduct was constitutionally protected under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Appellant participated in a demonstration in a residential neighborhood where appellant spoke over a portable public address system while a small group of people carried signs and picketed. Police arrived as a result of complaints about the noise. The officers informed appellant that his group could picket peacefully, but he had to discontinue use of the loud speaker. Appellant ignored repeated warnings and continued to use the loud speaker. The officers arrested appellant for disorderly conduct under 18 P.S. § 4406, and appellant was tried and convicted. Appellant sought review claiming that his conduct was constitutionally protected under U.S. Const. amend I. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of disorderly conduct finding that the disorderly conduct statute was constitutional. The statute did not forbid any specific speech, and it only regulated the volume at which speech could be delivered. Police had not deprived appellant of his First Amendment rights; appellant had been free to convey his message at a lower volume.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting appellant of disorderly conduct. The disorderly conduct statute did not forbid appellant's exercise of his First Amendment rights. The statute only regulated the volume at which speech was impressed upon the ears of the community. Appellant was properly convicted based on his conduct and his refusal to stop using a loud speaker following repeated warnings from the police.

Commonwealth v. Winkleman


No. 319, Oct. T., 1974


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


230 Pa. Super. 265; 326 A.2d 496; 1974 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2446


June 18, 1974, Submitted  
September 23, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, of Philadelphia, Miscellaneous Docket No. 73-00-2157, and M. C. No. 72-11-1713, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Victoria Ann Winkleman.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed and defendant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that convicted her of public indecency and obscene exhibition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a dancer performing at a nightclub. She was arrested after one of her dancing performances and charged under the Public Indecency Act, 18 P.S. § 4519, and the Obscene Exhibition Act, 18 P.S. § 4528. Defendant was convicted and a sentence was imposed. Defendant sought review of the judgment contending that her convictions must be reversed because the sections of Pennsylvania's previous crime code were unconstitutional as violative of U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV, in that the sections were overly broad and vague. The Commonwealth contended the sections were not constitutionally infirm since the defendant's dance was not conduct protected by the freedom of speech and expression provisions of the First Amendment as applied to the states by the Fourteenth Amendment. The court reversed the sentence and discharged defendant. The court found the statutes unconstitutional as applied to defendant in this particular case because § 4519 and § 4528 did not meet the Miller Test in that the statutes failed to set forth with specificity the type of conduct that was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the sentence of judgment and discharged the defendant because defendant's conduct came within the purview of the First Amendment and the Public Indecency statute did not specify what type of conduct was prohibited.

Commonwealth v. Stoffan


No. 388, April T., 1973


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


228 Pa. Super. 127; 323 A.2d 318; 1974 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1558


November 14, 1973, Argued  
June 21, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgments of sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County, Jan. T., 1973, No. 627A, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Stephen Stoffan.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence reversed and matter remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of illegally prescribing drugs, in violation of 35 P.S. § 780-113(a)(14).


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted of illegally prescribing drugs, defendant argued the evidence was insufficient to convict him because the prosecution failed to prove defendant dispensed the medication without a physical examination and without being satisfied that the patient was not drug-dependent. However, the prosecution argued these were exceptions to conviction and thus were affirmative defenses on which defendant bore the burden of proof. Reviewing the statute, the court held the clauses at issue were elements of the crime because the clauses were so incorporated with the language defining the offense itself that the ingredients of the offense could not be accurately described if the clauses were omitted. Additionally, the court held the element focusing on defendant's determination of whether the patient was not drug-dependent could be judged on a subjective standard for which expert testimony could be introduced. The court then held the prosecution failed to prove that defendant's encounters with the patient prior to prescribing the medication did not constitute a physical or visual examinations of the patient. Thus, the court remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions for illegally prescribing controlled substances because the evidence was insufficient to support the verdicts. The court then remanded the case for a new trial.
